### 3.1 Collision conventions
- All collisions are **circle vs circle** using wrap-aware `dist2` against squared radii. Polygon shapes are cosmetic.
- Pass order in `update()`: garbage pickup (during garbage update) → player bullets → targets; hostile bullets → ship → **chain nodes**; hazard bodies → ship (using a spread copy `[...arrays]` so `split()` pushes during iteration are safe); **hazard bodies → chain nodes** (spread copy, labeled `chainScan` loop, first hit wins per frame); saucer bullets → debris satellites.
- Entities are killed by setting `dead = true`; arrays are filtered once at the end of the frame. **Follow this pattern** — it avoids iterator invalidation bugs. (Exception: chain nodes are removed via `breakChain`/`chain.pop()`, never a dead flag — see 3.4.)
- Ship collision radius switches to `SHIELD_RADIUS` (26) whenever the shield is up. The shield does **not** extend to chain nodes (deliberate — see 2.10.1).
- Chain nodes use an effective radius of 7 vs hazard bodies and 9 vs hostile bullets.
- **Unshielded contact/bullet hits call `damageShip(amount, hazardX, hazardY)`** (v1.3) instead of the old instant-kill `killShip()`: it subtracts source-specific HP, applies knockback + a 1.0 s hit-stun, and only routes to `killShip()` (game over) at 0 HP. Shielded contact deflects/blocks instead (no damage). Because `damageShip` self-guards on shield/hit-stun/dead, the hazard-vs-ship loops no longer `break` after the first hit — a shielded ship still deflects every overlapping hazard, and an unshielded one absorbs exactly one hit per stun window (§2.12).

### 3.2 Rendering conventions
- `drawPoly(points, x, y, angle, color, closed)` + `glowStroke(color, width, blur)` produce the vector look via `shadowBlur`. New entities should define local-space point arrays and reuse these — don't invent per-entity draw pipelines. Canisters (free and chained) share one renderer, `drawCanister()`.
- `drawLink()` skips any link whose wrap-aware length exceeds 120 px — this prevents chain segments from streaking across the screen at the wrap seam. Keep this guard if touching chain rendering.
- `shadowBlur` is the main perf cost. If adding many simultaneous entities (>~80), consider a global glow toggle. The salvage feature adds up to ~12 chain nodes + ~15 free canisters at once; watch frame rate in garbage-heavy late waves.
- **No fills, except bullets/particles — plus two deliberate exceptions.** (1, v3.6 P1c) The Scoop capture box (§2.14.1) is drawn as a translucent `ctx.fill()` (`COLOR.dock`, alpha ≈0.15) with the usual `glowStroke` outline on top. It's a HUD-ish world-space affordance showing the exact `inScoopBox()` capture region, not an entity. (2, v3.6 P5) The **death-spectacle white flash** (§2.7/§2.9) is a full-viewport `ctx.fillRect` at decaying alpha, drawn in screen space after the world on the first frames of the `dying` state — a transient screen-wash, not an entity fill. The spectacle's **shockwave ring** stays inside the rule: it's a stroked `ctx.arc` via `glowStroke`, no fill. Neither exception is license to start filling entities generally; both are one-offs, named here so a future pass that doesn't know why they exist doesn't "fix" them away.

### 3.3 Known safe extension points
- **New enemy:** copy the `HunterSatellite` or `DebrisSatellite` class shape (constructor / update / draw / dead), add an array to `game`, wire into: `startGame` reset, `update()` entity update + collision passes + cleanup filter, `draw()` z-order, and wave-clear condition if it should block wave end. Decide explicitly whether it can damage the chain (add it to the `chainHazards` spread if so — as `game.hunters` is).
- **New weapon/powerup:** hook `Ship.update` fire block; bullets already carry a `hostile` flag that all collision passes respect. *v1.7 (F6) is the worked example:* weapon caps flow through `maxBullets()` (not the raw `MAX_BULLETS`) and Triple Shot's spread lives in the fire block; timed effects live in `game.powerFx` and count down in `update()`; the Engine/Magnet utility effects hook `chainMass()` and the garbage-pickup pass respectively (not parallel systems). Copy the `Powerup` class shape for any new pickup and add its cleanup filter + `update()` pickup pass.
- **New sound:** add an `AudioSys` method; one-shots follow `fire()`, loops follow `thrust()`.
- **New cargo-adjacent mechanic:** work through the existing chain functions — score through `addScore`, break through `breakChain`, convert nodes with `Garbage.fromNode`.

### 3.4 Chain physics contract (v1.1) — read before touching `updateChain`

The tow chain is the only physics system in the game that is *not* the standard entity pattern. Its rules:

- **Node shape:** plain objects `{ x, y, px, py, spin, spinRate, mass }` in the `game.chain` array, ordered head (nearest ship) → tail. `px/py` are the previous-frame verlet positions; implied velocity is `(x−px, y−py)`. **`mass`** (v1.4/F5) is copied from the picked-up `Garbage` (default 1.0) and drives the handling penalties — **any code that creates a chain node must set `mass`**, or `chainMass()` will `NaN`. There is no `dead` flag and no class — nodes are created inline at pickup and removed only by `breakChain(i)`, `scatterChain()`, or `chain.pop()` at the dock.
- **Integration order per frame** (inside `updateChain`): (1) verlet integrate all nodes with damping `0.18^dt`; (2) measure the **pre-constraint** stretch of the first link and apply the momentum tug to the ship; (3) run `CHAIN_ITER` (4, was 3) relaxation passes of position-based distance constraints (link 0: node takes 100% of the correction, the anchor is kinematic; links 1+: 50/50 split between neighbor nodes); (4) `wrapNode` every node.
- **Why tug-before-constraints:** the pre-constraint stretch is the honest measure of how much the cargo resisted the ship this frame. Applying a spring force *after* constraints (when stretch ≈ 0) does nothing; applying stiff springs *instead of* constraints oscillates. Don't reorder these steps.
- **Wrap handling:** `wrapNode` shifts `px/py` by the same amount as `x/y` so implied velocity survives the teleport — this is why the chain doesn't explode at screen edges. All link deltas (constraints *and* rendering) go through `shortDelta`. Any new code measuring between two nodes must do the same.
- **Constraints are equality (rod-like), not rope-like** (they also correct compression). This is what produces the serpentine follow instead of nodes bunching on the ship when it decelerates. If you change to stretch-only constraints, expect the snake feel to disappear.
- **Cargo penalties live in `Ship.update`**, not in the chain code: `thrustMul` and `maxSp` are computed from **`chainMass()`** (Σ node.mass, v1.4/F5), and the momentum-tug `massFactor` in `updateChain` uses the same sum. Before v1.4 these used `game.chain.length` (a count); for all-mass-1.0 cargo the sum equals the count, so v1.3 balance is preserved. If you add other cargo effects (turn rate, shield drain), put them in `Ship.update` alongside and scale them off `chainMass()` too.
- **Stability envelope:** re-validated for v3.4 P1 at dt ≤ 0.05 (the main-loop clamp), **`CARGO_CAP_MAX` (**24**, up from 20) nodes, `CHAIN_ITER` (4) constraint iterations** (unchanged — re-validated, not assumed). Headless stress (`scratchpad/test-p6.js` (E)): a **24-node** chain under hard thrust-flips across a wrap, 900 frames, shows no NaN, no velocity explosion, and worst-case link stretch ≈**4.11 px** on a 20 px link — under the ~5 px budget, so `CHAIN_ITER` did **not** need to bump to 5 (measured directly: at 4 iters 4.11 px, at 5 iters 3.67 px — both comfortably stable, 4 was kept). This is barely above the prior 20-node measurement (~4 px), consistent with B-8's iteration count already carrying headroom past 20 nodes. The worst link is link 0 (anchor→head, dominated by ship speed), not the tail, so corrections propagate the full length — the chain doesn't sag. If you lengthen the chain or the link length further, revalidate the same way (see 5.4 rule 7) before shipping; the `drawLink` 120 px wrap-skip still reads correctly at 24 nodes.

---

## 4. Enhancement Roadmap (candidate backlog)

> **The large v2.0 feature set** (controller support, HP system, powerups, achievements, a larger scrolling world, and the satellite redesigns) **has now shipped** — its specs live in Section 2, and its retired planning docs are in `archive/` (see `archive/README.md`). Items below that overlapped with v2.0 are struck through; the rest remain a candidate backlog for a future cycle.

> **v3.0 (complete, archived — specs in `archive/PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.md`, build order in `archive/IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.md`; all 8 phases SHIPPED, "Phase 9" never existed).** The v3.0 change set was an **achievements overhaul** — the **tier infrastructure + converting the seven flagged lifetime achievements into 6-tier bronze→diamond ladders (`afd_achievements_v2`), Phase 7**, and the **seven new tiered lifetime/event achievements (Sharpshooter, Freight Baron, Zen Master, Daredevil, Wave Rider, Salvage King, Field Sweeper) + the new "Flawless Run" weekly (16-pool rotation), Phase 8** (§2.17) — plus **Orbital Overhaul Change Set 1**: (1/2) reach the pause/Options/Achievements menu from *any* state via ESC or keyboard O / controller B, with Start still pausing during play — Phase 4; (3) a more legible starfield/parallax motion reference — Phase 1; (4/5) a new **Options → Difficulty** screen letting shot powerups expire by shots and the Magnet by pieces collected, not only by time — Phase 5; (6) a fire-rate rebalance (slower base gun, genuinely faster Rapid Fire) — Phase 2; (7) a HUD "targets remaining" count — Phase 3; (8) a growing tow-cargo cap (12 → 20) with a chain physics retune — Phase 6. All documented in Section 2 (§2.9, §2.10.2, §2.11, §2.14, §2.15, §2.16, §2.17).
>
> **v3.4 (in progress — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.4.md`, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.4.md`; Phase 1 SHIPPED).** Change set: economy & dock tuning — **Hunter garbage drops now scale by tier** (`HUNTER_GARBAGE` a `{3,2,1}` table replacing the flat rate + `HUNTER_SMALL_GARBAGE`), `DEBRIS_GARBAGE` 3→4 to compensate field-side (§2.4, §2.5); **dock intake rate** hoisted to `DOCK_OFFLOAD_INTERVAL` (0.13→0.05 s, was a bare literal — §2.10); **tow capacity** `CARGO_CAP_MAX` 20→24 without re-solving the mass-penalty coefficients (a bigger hold costs more handling by design), with the chain stability envelope re-validated at 24 nodes rather than assumed (§2.10.1, §2.10.2, §3.4) — **SHIPPED, Phase 1**. **Considered and declined for this round: rectangular dock capture geometry** (an oriented box like the Scoop's mouth, §2.14, instead of the circular `DOCK_RADIUS+10` zone) — the circular zone reads fine at the current radius and wasn't in this round's scope; revisit only if playtest specifically flags dock approach-angle friction as a problem.
>
> **v3.1 (in progress — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.1.md`, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES.md`; Phase 2 of N SHIPPED).** Change set: (1) **shrink the toroidal world** 3840×2160→2560×1440 with matching spawn/dock ring clamps — **SHIPPED, Phase 1** (§2.11); (2) **fix the `+120` wrap-jump discontinuity** so entities teleport by exactly `WORLD_W`/`WORLD_H` — **SHIPPED, Phase 2** (§2.11); (3) mutual garbage magnetism + coalescence (12 loose canisters can clump into a Hunter, with a warning cue) — next. See `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.1.md` / `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES.md` for full specs and remaining phases.

Ordered roughly by effort. Each is scoped to fit a single working session.

**Small (one short session)**
1. **High-score persistence** — in-memory top-5 table with initials entry on game over. (Note: localStorage does not work in claude.ai artifact preview; fine in a real browser. Gate it with a try/catch.)
2. **Screen shake + flash** on ship death and satellite kill. Add `game.shake` timer, offset ctx translate in `draw()`.
3. **Thump-synced pulse** — starfield or border glow pulses with the heartbeat.
4. ~~**Gamepad support**~~ → shipped in v1.8 (v2.0 Feature F7); see §2.15.

**Medium (one full session)**
5. ~~**Power-up drops**~~ → shipped in v1.7 (v2.0 Feature F6); see §2.14.
6. **Debris Satellite variants** — e.g. "dense" units (2 hits, darker stroke), "volatile" units (explode, damaging neighbors in radius). Add a `type` field to `DebrisSatellite`; keep circle collision. A "hot" variant could drop extra canisters. *F3 (Debris Satellites) has now shipped (v1.4) — this would layer on top of it: a per-type branch in `destroyDebris` and the constructor.*
7. **Boss saucer every 5 waves** — large multi-hit saucer with a visible hull-damage state (drop polygon vertices as it takes hits). Could deliberately target the player's tow chain for extra menace.
8. **Attract mode** — after 15 s idle on title, run a simple AI demo game (rotate toward nearest rock, thrust away from close threats, fire).

**Large (multi-session — split into sub-goals)**
9. **Two-player co-op** (shared screen, second ship on IJKL/etc., friendly-fire toggle).
10. **Touch controls** for mobile — virtual buttons in the letterbox margins; ties into the existing scaling code.
11. **Campaign structure** — named sectors with modifier rules (gravity well at center, asteroid belts that spawn from one edge, "no shield" sector, etc.).

---

## 5. Session Handoff Protocol

This mirrors the Atomic Dustbin Dan workflow: each new Claude session gets three attachments and a short kickoff prompt.

### 5.1 What to attach to every new session
1. **`asteroids-deluxe.html`** — the current build (always the latest working version).
2. **This GDD** — or at minimum Sections 1–3 plus whichever Section 4 item is being built.
3. **`STATUS.md`** — the running status document (template below). Update it at the end of every session.
4. **For a v3.0 phase:** attach `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.md` and `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES.md` (both at the repo root) and paste that phase's ready-to-paste prompt. The v2.0 planning docs remain archived under `archive/` (historical reference only, not active specs). When all v3.0 phases ship, these v3.0 docs archive the same way — Section 2 + `STATUS.md` stay authoritative.

### 5.2 Kickoff prompt template

> I'm continuing development of Asteroid Field Deluxe, a single-file HTML5 vector arcade game. Attached: the current build, the game design document, and the status doc.
>
> Read the GDD's Architecture Map (Section 3) before writing code — especially the wrap-aware collision helpers, the dead-flag/filter lifecycle, and the tuning-constants convention.
>
> **This session's goal:** [one specific item, e.g. "Roadmap item 5: power-up drops — rapid fire and shield overcharge only"]
>
> Constraints: keep it a single self-contained HTML file, no external assets or libraries, all changes consistent with the design pillars in GDD Section 1. Deliver the full updated file plus a summary of what changed for the status doc.

### 5.3 STATUS.md template

```markdown
# Asteroid Field Deluxe — STATUS
Last updated: [date] · Build version: [x.y] · Last session: [one line]

## Working / verified
- [features confirmed working in a real browser]

## Known issues
- [bugs, with repro steps if known]

## Balance notes
- [tuning observations from playtesting, e.g. "small wedges feel unfair at turnRate 2.6"]

## Next up
- [the next roadmap item, plus any prep notes]

## Changed this session
- [diff-level summary a future session can trust without re-reading everything]
```

### 5.4 Rules for future sessions (instructions to Claude)

Any Claude session working on this project should:

1. **Deliver the complete file, not fragments.** The build must always be runnable as-is. If the file grows too large for a single response, deliver it in clearly-marked sequential parts and reassemble instructions.
2. **Preserve the tuning-constants convention.** New mechanics get named constants at the top of the script, never inline magic numbers.
3. **Use the wrap-aware helpers** (`dist2`, `angleTo`) for all distance and aiming math. This is the most common way to introduce subtle bugs.
4. **Follow the entity lifecycle**: `dead` flag + end-of-frame `.filter()`. Never remove entities mid-iteration.
5. **Respect the design pillars** (Section 1). If a requested feature conflicts with a pillar, say so and propose an alternative before building.
6. **Route all scoring through `addScore()`** so extra-life logic stays correct.
7. **Syntax-check AND functionally test before delivering.** Extract the script block and run `node --check`. For gameplay logic, use the headless harness pattern established in v1.1: stub `window`, `document.getElementById` (returning a canvas whose `getContext` yields a Proxy that no-ops all methods), and `requestAnimationFrame`; then drive `startGame()` and `update(1/60)` directly, teleporting the ship to set up scenarios. AudioSys is safe headless because every method early-returns when `this.ctx` is null (init only fires on keydown). Verified this way in v1.1: pickup, tow constraint length, screen-wrap chain integrity, dock delivery scoring, and chain severing.
8. **Version bump + changelog.** Increment the version comment at the top of the file and produce a "Changed this session" summary for STATUS.md.
9. **Don't refactor unprompted.** Paul knows this codebase; large structural rewrites make session-to-session diffs unreadable. Propose refactors, don't spring them.
10. **Flag playtest asks.** Claude can't play the game — end each session with 2–3 specific things Paul should verify in the browser (e.g. "confirm the new power-up despawns after 8 s").

---

## 6. Bug Watch List (v1.1)

Areas most likely to hide issues, worth checking during playtests:

- **Shield-deflection edge cases** — deflecting a rock into a wall of other rocks; deflecting at exactly the moment energy hits zero. New in v1.1: deflecting a rock directly into your own tow chain (working as designed, but verify it feels fair).
- ~~**Respawn deadlock**~~ — *resolved by F2 (v1.3): there is no respawn anymore, so this can't occur.*
- **Knockback vs. tow chain (v1.3)** — knockback shoves the ship away from a hazard, which can drag a long chain tail through *other* hazards or fling it across the wrap seam. The chain is wrap-aware and severs per its existing rules, but verify a hit never yanks the ship somewhere that instantly severs the whole haul unfairly.
- **Knockback into a second hazard (v1.3)** — the 1.0 s hit-stun means being knocked straight into another rock is safe *during* the window; verify it doesn't feel like the ship pinballs helplessly once the window expires in a dense field.
- **Saucer sound leak** — the warble is stopped on saucer death/exit and on game over; verify it can't persist if a saucer dies the same frame the ship does.
- **Performance (raised in v1.4, again in v1.6; revisited v3.3 P4, v3.4 P1)** — heavy `shadowBlur`; the salvage feature already raised the entity ceiling, and F3's guaranteed per-tier drops raise the *free-canister* count far higher (a fully-cleared Debris large lineage emits **52** as of v3.4 P1's `DEBRIS_GARBAGE` 3→4 bump; a fully-cleared Hunter lineage — of **any** origin as of v3.3 P4 9b — now emits **18**, down from a flat-rate 66 now that v3.4 P1 made `HUNTER_GARBAGE` a per-tier table, so Hunter lineages are no longer the larger of the two sources). **v3.3 P4 reintroduced single-garbage decay** (`GARBAGE_DECAY` ≈ 22 s, singles only), which caps how much standing salvage accumulates even with every Hunter emitting again; clumps persist. Render is viewport-culled (`onScreen` in `drawEntity`), so free-canister count doesn't drive *draw* cost; the O(n²) `coalesceGarbage` pass is the watch item (FLAG D-2 — cheap pair tests, survivable, and coalescence compacts `n` downward; v3.4 P1's net drop-volume change is a modest reduction, not an increase, so this doesn't get worse). Watch frame time at wave 10+; if it dips, a global glow toggle (§3.2) is the lever, then the drop-volume constants (`DEBRIS_GARBAGE` / `HUNTER_GARBAGE`), then (only if a stress test shows it) a spatial hash for the coalescence pass — explicitly out of scope until then.
- **Hunter shield-kill at point-blank (v1.6)** — destroying a medium Hunter on the shield spawns 3 smalls right at the shield edge; they scatter outward for 0.6 s before homing, so it *shouldn't* be an instant point-blank swarm, but verify it feels fair (a fair "spend energy, but now deal with the smalls" trade, not a death trap) — this is the old wedge tension carried forward.
- **Hunter early-game feel vs. escalation (v1.6)** — the whole family moves at `HUNTER_FLOOR_FRAC` (0.58) of full speed at wave 1. Verify the large core's drift and any split children genuinely feel *gentle* in the opening waves (not still-too-fast) and that both tier-climb and wave-climb read as a smooth escalation, not a cliff. `HUNTER_FLOOR_FRAC` (family-wide early calm) and `RAMP_WAVES` (whole-game pace) are the knobs.
- **Garbage density & the re-tuned coalescence economy (v3.3 P4, SUPERSEDES the permanent-salvage ask)** — single decay is back and the whole coalescence economy was re-tuned around it. The open questions: with `GARBAGE_DECAY` (≈ 22 s), `GARBAGE_COALESCE_DELAY` (≈ 3.0 s), and `GARBAGE_MAGNET_RANGE` (≈ 180) all moved together, do clumps still form *at all* before singles age out — or does decay now starve coalescence (if so, cut the delay or lengthen decay)? Post-9b (every Hunter drops again), does the field **silt up** or does decay hold it through late waves? Does the reddening clump hull read as "shoot me" **or** now "scoop me" (both are correct)? And is the **scoop vs. shatter** choice live — do you sometimes shatter for a lossless comeback rather than greedily scoop and waste the overflow? These are the top v3.3 P4 retune asks; the `nextWave` `min(3+wave,9)` count / `SPAWN_MAX_DIST` are the direct levers if the late-wave lull persists (§9 preamble).
- **Powerup drop rate & Magnet feel (v1.7/F6)** — `POWERUP_DROP_CHANCE` (10%) and the ambient `POWERUP_HEALTH_GAP` (18–26 s) are first-pass, no playtest data. Verify drops feel *earned but not stingy* (not so rare they never matter, not so common they stop feeling special), and that the Magnet's pull reads as a satisfying sweep rather than jittery orbiting (levers: `MAGNET_PULL` up-front accel, `MAGNET_DAMP` in-range damping — lower `MAGNET_DAMP` toward 0 to make it settle harder, or drop `MAGNET_PULL` if garbage zips/overshoots). Also confirm the five icons read distinctly at a glance and the HUD duration row is legible.
- **Controller feel & audio unlock (v1.8/F7)** — the binding *logic* is headless-verified, but deadzone comfort, whether right-trigger *or* right-bumper is the right shield button (a gap-fill, not spec'd), and general button-mapping feel can only be judged with a real controller in a browser — **the top v1.8 playtest ask.** `GP_DEADZONE` (0.25) is the one feel knob. Also verify: does the D-Pad-vs-stick split feel natural; does Start pausing/unpausing read cleanly; and — since browsers don't reliably treat gamepad input as an audio-autoplay gesture — does a controller-only start produce sound, or is one keyboard press still needed to unlock audio? (If the latter, that's a known browser limitation, not a bug.)
- **Menu feel & first-time persistence (v1.9/F8)** — the menu *logic* is headless-verified (40 assertions), but three things need a real browser: (1) does menu navigation feel natural on **keyboard and gamepad** (slider granularity at `VOL_STEP` 0.1; edge-detected one-press-one-move gamepad nav vs. wanting held auto-repeat); (2) does a rebound control take effect **immediately** in live play, and are the two flagged quirks acceptable — a gamepad rebind **dropping that action's stick axis**, and **no conflict detection** when rebinding to an already-used key; (3) **do settings actually persist across a real reload** — this is the first feature to write `localStorage`, which is absent in the artifact sandbox, so real persistence is unverified (worst case in the sandbox is "no persistence," never a crash — access is guarded). See §2.16.
- **Chain tug oscillation** — `CHAIN_TUG 26` is stable in headless tests but hasn't been feel-tested against every input pattern. Rapid thrust-flip-thrust with a full chain is the stress case; if the ship judders, lower `CHAIN_TUG` before touching the constraint code.
- ~~**Dock/respawn interaction**~~ — *moot post-F2 (v1.3): no respawn. `killShip()` still calls `scatterChain()`, so a dead ship never keeps a chain.*
- **Wave-transition cargo** — the chain persists across waves (deliberate) but new large debris satellites spawn ≥220 px from the *ship*; a long chain tail can extend beyond that. Verify a wave spawn can't instantly sever a fresh chain unfairly often.
- **Delivery combo reset radius** — combo resets at dock radius+40. Verify a player orbiting the dock edge can't accidentally keep/lose the combo in a confusing way.

---

## 7. Version History

- **v1.0** — Initial build: ship/asteroids/saucers, shield, killer satellite + homing wedges, waves, synth audio.
- **v1.1** — Radioactive salvage: garbage drops with decay, verlet tow chain (mass/momentum penalties, momentum tug), chain vulnerability with aft-severing, relocating recycling dock with escalating delivery scores, cargo HUD + dock pointer, pickup/deliver SFX. New constants block; `shortDelta` helper; `Garbage`/`FloatText`/`Dock` classes; chain physics functions after `shieldDeflect`. Headless-tested: pickup, tow, wrap, delivery scoring, severing.
- **v1.2** — *v2.0 Phase 1 (F1): Larger scrolling world & camera.* Simulation space split from the screen: a 3840×2160 toroidal world (`WORLD_W/H`) with a 1280×720 viewport (`VIEW_W/H`) that scrolls to keep the ship centered (`game.camera`). All wrap-aware helpers (`wrap`/`dist2`/`angleTo`/`shortDelta`/`wrapNode`) retargeted to `WORLD_*`; added `wrapOffset`/`wrapPos`. `draw()` gained a camera transform, wrap-aware per-entity nearest-image rendering + viewport culling (`onScreen`/`drawEntity`), and a world-spanning seamless starfield; HUD/overlays drawn screen-fixed after restore. Spawns (wave asteroids, dock) now ship-relative rings; satellites/saucers enter from viewport edges relative to the ship (feel unchanged). New constants: `CULL_MARGIN`, `SPAWN_MIN/MAX_DIST`, `DOCK_MIN/MAX_DIST`, `STAR_DENSITY`. Headless-tested: camera-follow, world-boundary wrap (x & y), no wrap at old 1280 boundary, ship-relative spawn reachability across the seam, draw() crash-free in all states.
- **v1.3** — *v2.0 Phase 2 (F2): Health Points & Knockback.* Discrete lives replaced by a single HP pool (`SHIP_MAX_HP` = 250) for the whole run; all respawn/lives logic removed (`game.lives`/`nextExtraLife`/`respawnTimer` gone, plus the "respawn only when center is clear" gate). New `damageShip()` handles unshielded hits: source-specific damage (`DMG_SMALL/MEDIUM/LARGE` 20/35/50, `DMG_BULLET` 15, via each hazard's new `damage` field), a `KNOCKBACK_SPEED` (250 px/s) shove away from the hazard, and a `HIT_STUN_DURATION` (1.0 s) i-frame window (reusing `ship.invuln`). `killShip()` is now a respawn-free game over at 0 HP. `addScore()` milestone changed from extra-life to a +25 HP hull repair (`REPAIR_*`), converting to a flat score bonus at full HP. HUD: HULL/HP bar (`COLOR.hp`) replaces the life-ship icons, styled like the shield bar. New `AudioSys.hit()` damage thud. Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-f2.js`, 54 assertions): per-hit-type damage, hit-stun double-hit prevention, knockback direction/magnitude, 0-HP game over with no respawn, milestone repair, and shield still blocking damage+knockback.
- **v1.4** — *v2.0 Phase 3 (F3 Debris Satellites + F5 variable-mass garbage).* The `Asteroid` class → **`DebrisSatellite`** (array `game.asteroids` → `game.debris`; `AST_*` constants → `DEBRIS_*`; `destroyAsteroid` → `destroyDebris`; `COLOR.asteroid` → `COLOR.debris`); redrawn as a broken-satellite silhouette (irregular `hull` polygon + 1–2 antenna/panel `shards`). Splits changed to 3-way at large/medium (small destroyed), and **every** tier's destruction emits exactly `DEBRIS_GARBAGE` (3) canisters — replacing the probabilistic `GARBAGE_DROP` — so a fully-cleared large lineage yields 39 canisters. F5: `Garbage` and chain nodes gained a **`mass`** field (default 1.0); `Garbage.fromNode()` carries it, pickup copies it onto the node, and the chain thrust/top-speed penalties + momentum-tug `massFactor` now scale off **`chainMass()`** (Σ node.mass) instead of `chain.length` — identical feel for all-mass-1.0 cargo, the groundwork for F4's low-mass Hunter scrap. First-pass balance for the ~8× garbage volume: `GARBAGE_DECAY` 20→12, new `GARBAGE_SEVER_DECAY` 10 (was inline 15), wave spawn `min(4+w,11)`→`min(3+w,9)`. Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-f3.js`, 28 assertions): 39-canister lineage count, per-tier splits, mass propagation (default/fromNode/pickup/sever), and the mass-sum equivalence of an 8× mass-1.0 chain vs a 16× mass-0.5 chain across thrust, top speed, and tug.
- **v1.5** — *v2.0 Phase 4 (F10 difficulty ramp + saucer calming).* A global difficulty ramp: `difficultyFactor(wave)` = `1 − e^(−(wave−1)/RAMP_WAVES)` (0 at wave 1, → 1 over many waves; `RAMP_WAVES` = 8 is the single ramp knob) and a `ramp(floor, ceil, wave)` interpolation helper, both in the Helpers block. The **saucers** are re-expressed as floor/ceiling pairs scaled through `ramp` (§2.6, §2.13): spawn gap `rand(20,30)s` → `rand(12,16)s` (re-expressing the old `rand(12,22)−min(6,wave)`); a fire-rate multiplier `1.8×` → `1.0×` applied via a new `Saucer.rollFireTimer(range)` to both saucers' reloads and first-shot delay; small-saucer aim error `±0.35` → `±0.09` rad; and small-saucer appearance chance `15%` → `60%`, which **folds in** (replaces) the old score>8000 gate so escalation is wave-driven in one place. Pillar 6 ("Ease players in") flipped from planned to shipped. No behavior/shape changes; the Hunter Satellite (§2.5) and Debris-density scaling are deferred to their own phases. Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-f4.js`, 30 assertions): the `difficultyFactor` curve shape across waves 1–25, and each saucer parameter (gap/fire/aim/chance) at wave 1 vs wave 20 in the right direction and magnitude — including end-to-end through a real `Saucer`'s fired-bullet aim error and `rollFireTimer`.
- **v1.6** — *v2.0 Phase 5 (F4 Hunter Satellites).* The killer `Satellite` + homing `Wedge` classes were merged into one **`HunterSatellite`** class — a teal diamond family with three tiers (3 large / 2 medium / 1 small). The large core drifts passively toward the ship (spawn-time aim, no re-aim) and, when shot, splits **3-ways** into medium then small children that actively home (wrap-aware, relentless), each faster/more agile than the last; splits/garbage run through a new **`destroyHunter`** (parallel to `destroyDebris`), and a `static spawnCore()` places the off-edge large. **Every speed and turn rate wires into the v1.5 difficulty ramp from the start**: each is `ramp(ceiling × HUNTER_FLOOR_FRAC, ceiling, wave)` (ceilings 70 drift / 120·1.6 medium / 175·2.6 small; `HUNTER_FLOOR_FRAC` = 0.58), sampled at spawn — so the whole family moves at ~60% speed at wave 1, ramping to ~96% by wave 20. Garbage at every tier: 3 normal-mass (1.0) at large/medium; a burst of `HUNTER_SMALL_GARBAGE` (6) **low-mass** (0.5) canisters at small, rendered in a paler tint (`COLOR.garbageLight`) as an easy-to-tow bonus. Contact damage 60/45/30 by tier (`HUNTER_DAMAGE`, above the equivalent Debris tier). Shield: the core bounces, homers are destroyed on contact and still split; Hunters still sever the tow chain. Removed `SAT_SCORE`/`WEDGE_SCORE`; added the `HUNTER_*` constants block. Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-f5.js`, 40 assertions): full-lineage 13 kills / 66-canister tiered-mass count, per-tier splits & garbage mass, damage/score tables, the difficulty ramp on every tier (wave-1 floor vs wave-20), active-homing re-aim, and chain-severing on contact; f2/f3/f4 regressions updated to the merged entity and re-run green.
- **v1.7** — *v2.0 Phase 6 (F6 Powerups).* Five free-floating pickups via a new **`Powerup`** class (rotating-hexagon housing + a distinct per-type glyph through the shared `drawPowerupGlyph()`, reused by the HUD). **Health** spawns ambiently on a saucer-like timer (`POWERUP_HEALTH_GAP`, one at a time) and instantly repairs +25 HP capped; **Rapid Fire / Triple Shot / Magnet / Engine** drop from small-tier Debris/Hunter kills at `POWERUP_DROP_CHANCE` (10%) via `maybeDropPowerup()` and last `POWERUP_DURATION` (15 s). Rapid raises the bullet cap 4→8; Triple fires a 3-bullet `TRIPLE_SPREAD` fan and raises it 4→12 — both active takes the higher cap (12), not 24, via the new `maxBullets()` the fire block now reads. Magnet pulls free garbage toward the ship inside `MAGNET_RANGE_MULT`×`GARBAGE_PICKUP` (with `MAGNET_DAMP` so it glides) and widens the pickup radius; Engine halves the effective towed mass by applying `ENGINE_MASS_MULT` inside `chainMass()`, so thrust/top-speed/tug all lighten. Same-type pickups refresh the timer (`game.powerFx`) rather than stacking; a HUD row shows each active timed effect with a shield-bar-style duration bar; new `AudioSys.powerup()` chime. Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-f6.js`, 39 assertions): effect magnitudes + duration expiry, the 12-not-24 combined cap, the triple-shot spread and rapid cap driven through the real fire block, Engine's `chainMass` halving, the Magnet moving garbage toward the ship over frames (and not when inactive), and small-tier-only drops (never large, never Health); f2/f3/f4/f5 regressions re-run green.
- **v1.8** — *v2.0 Phase 7 (F7 Controller Support).* Gamepad input layered onto the keyboard with **no call-site changes** — `input.left()`/`thrust()`/etc. now resolve keyboard **or** the first connected gamepad through a single data-driven **`bindings`** table (per-action keyboard `keys` / gamepad `buttons` / analog `axis` + a `fixed` rebindable flag), so Phase 8's rebinding UI has one structure to build against. `pollGamepad()` snapshots `navigator.getGamepads()[first-connected]` once per frame before `update()` (ignoring extra pads); `input.*()` resolves held-state lazily from that snapshot via `actionHeld`/`kbActive`/`gpActive`. Defaults (F7 spec): D-Pad / Left Stick rotate + thrust past a `GP_DEADZONE` (0.25), A fires, right trigger/bumper raises the shield (**a gap-fill — no controller shield was spec'd**). Fixed menu/system reads wired now for later phases via edge-triggered `gpPressed`: A = confirm, B = back (reserved for F8), Start = start/pause/unpause (Start toggles pause exactly like `P` today); the keyboard menu handler now reads the same `bindings.confirm`/`bindings.pause` entries. **Hardcoded defaults only — the rebinding UI is Phase 8 (F8).** Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-f7.js`, 52 assertions): keyboard-path regression, each default button/axis resolving to its action, the 0.25 deadzone (including the strict boundary), keyboard-OR-gamepad combining, first-pad-only selection, edge-triggered Start/A menu behavior (single-toggle, confirm-on-title/gameover, no restart mid-play), the binding-table data matching spec, and a gamepad thrust driving the real `Ship.update` through the unchanged input layer; f2–f6 regressions re-run green. See §2.15.
- **v1.9** — *v2.0 Phase 8 (F8 Pause Modal, Options Menu & Control Rebinding).* The game's first nested menu/UI state machine (§2.16): pause (`P` / gamepad Start) opens a modal (Continue / Options / Quit), Options has SFX/Music/Master volume sliders + a Controls rebinding screen, all navigable by keyboard **or** gamepad through a single `menuInput(action)` dispatcher. `game.menu {screen,index,row,col,rebinding}` holds the cursor/capture state; `game.paused` ⇔ a menu is open, toggled only by `openPause`/`closePause`/`quitToTitle` (Quit → title). **AudioSys refactored to a gain-routing graph** — every voice now connects to an `sfx` bus → `master` bus → speakers, with `setVol(cat,v)` driving the sliders (`vol {master,sfx,music}`); a `music` gain node exists but **nothing is connected to it — there is no music track** (the slider is wired for a future one, not a placeholder; §2.8). **Live rebinding**: selecting a binding cell and confirming captures the next key/button into `bindings[action]` (a gamepad rebind drops the analog axis); **Return to Defaults** restores the five `fixed:false` actions to `DEFAULT_BINDINGS` (a pristine pre-load snapshot). The `keydown` handler and `handleGamepadMenu` each resolve **three contexts in priority order — rebind-capture, menu-open, normal-play** — so menu/capture input can never leak into `keys{}` or ship control, and `update()` stays frozen while paused. Settings persist to `localStorage` (`afd_settings_v1`), all access `typeof`-guarded + try/caught so a storage failure never crashes. New `AudioSys.ui()` menu blip. Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-f8.js`, 40 assertions): the state-machine transitions, volume sliders driving both `vol` and the gain nodes with [0,1] clamping, live keyboard/gamepad rebind taking effect via `input.*()` with **no leak into gameplay keys** + frozen-while-paused, edge-detected gamepad nav, Return-to-Defaults exact restore, and a `localStorage` persistence round-trip; f2–f7 regressions re-run green. **Not yet browser-verified: real-`localStorage` persistence outside the artifact sandbox, and the menu feel/rebind-in-play playtest asks (STATUS.md).** See §2.16.
- **v2.0** — *v2.0 Phase 9 (F9 Achievements System) — v2.0 complete.* A progress-tracking layer that OBSERVES stats the rest of the game already produces (kill counts by hazard type/tier, dock deliveries, HP thresholds, powerup usage, wave reached, damage-free waves, play time) via light one-liner hooks at each event's existing site — no new indirection. Two pools via a single `Achievements` module: **15 weekly** (a calendar-deterministic 5-wide slice active each ISO week — pool index `(isoYear*52 + isoWeek) % 15`, 5 consecutive wrapping — so every player worldwide sees the same 5 on the same days; a new week resets weekly unlocks) and **12 lifetime** (cumulative across games). Per-game counters live in a flat `game.stats` bag (`resetGameStats()`); lifetime counters + unlock sets persist to their own `localStorage` key (`afd_achievements_v1`), guarded + try/caught like F8. An unlock pops a non-blocking gold **toast** (`AudioSys.achievement()` fanfare, aged out in the main loop by `updateToasts`) and is browsable in a read-only **viewer** at Pause → Options → Achievements (`drawAchievements`, this week's 5 + the 12 lifetime with unlock status + `cur/goal` progress). `Achievements.evaluate()` runs each frame (already-unlocked short-circuit) + once at game over (for end-of-game checks like Waste Not). Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-f9.js`, 62 assertions): ISO-week math incl. a year-boundary (2027-01-01 → ISO 2026-W53), the deterministic 5-slice + wrap-around, weekly-reset-on-new-week + lifetime-retained persistence round-trips, and real-driven gameplay unlocks at exact thresholds (15 debris kills, a 12+8 dock-delivery run, a sub-10-HP Hunter collision, all-four powerups, a full 13-kill Hunter lineage, a damage-free wave 3, and every lifetime just-below/at-goal boundary) + toast lifecycle; f2–f8 regressions re-run green. See GDD §2.17. **This ships the full v2.0 feature set (Phases 1–9).**
- **v2.0 feature set (Phases 1–9, complete)** — larger scrolling world (v1.2); HP & knockback (v1.3); Debris Satellites + variable-mass garbage (v1.4); difficulty ramp + saucer calming (v1.5); Hunter Satellite redesign (v1.6); powerups (v1.7); controller support (v1.8); pause/options menu + control rebinding (v1.9); achievements (v2.0). Still open (a tuning pass, not a feature): the joint F3+F10 Debris-density retune — see STATUS.md.
- **v3.0** — specs archived in `archive/PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.md`, build order in `archive/IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.md`. Change set: an achievements overhaul — **P7** the 6-tier bronze→diamond ladder infrastructure + conversion of the seven flagged lifetime achievements (`afd_achievements_v2` + `_v1` migration), and **P8** the seven new tiered lifetime/event achievements (Sharpshooter, Freight Baron, Zen Master, Daredevil, Wave Rider, Salvage King, Field Sweeper) + the new "Flawless Run" weekly (16-pool rotation) + the definition audit — both landed (§2.17) — and Orbital Overhaul Change Set 1: P1 starfield/parallax legibility (§2.11), P2 fire-rate rebalance (§2.2), P3 targets-remaining HUD (§2.7), P4 pause/menu-from-any-state + ESC-to-pause (§2.9/§2.16), P5 Difficulty Options screen with shot-count / pieces-collected powerup expiry modes (§2.14/§2.16), and **P6 (B-8) a growing tow-cargo cap (12→20) with a chain physics retune** (§2.10/§2.10.2/§3.4). P6: the fixed `CHAIN_MAX` became a runtime `game.cargoMax` that grows +1 per `CARGO_GROW_PER` (30) canisters delivered up to `CARGO_CAP_MAX` (20); the mass-penalty coefficients were softened (`CARGO_THRUST` 0.10→0.06, `CARGO_MAXSPD` 0.05→0.03, `CARGO_MASS` 0.12→0.07) so a full chain at the new ceiling matches the old full-12 feel (~45% thrust / ~63% top speed) rather than the "broken" ~33%/50% a naive m=20 gives, and `CHAIN_ITER` (relaxation passes) went 3→4 for stability at 20 nodes (stress-revalidated per §3.4 rule 7). Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-p6.js`, 37 assertions): cap starts at 12, grows +1/30-delivered up to and never past 20 (driven through real deliveries) with a "TOW +1" float, pickup gate + HUD read `cargoMax`, the retuned thrust/top-speed ratios measured through the real `Ship.update` (incl. Engine-at-20 ≡ plain-10 and the 0.07 tug coeff), and 20-node constraint stability across thrust-flips + a wrap (no NaN/explosion, worst link ≈4 px). Also fixed the long-standing `test-f3` Engine-drop flake. **v3.0 ended at Phase 8 — "Phase 9" never existed; the next cycle is v3.1** (`PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.1.md` / `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES.md`).
- **v3.1 (shipped)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.1.md`, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES.md`. **P1: shrink the toroidal world** `WORLD_W/H` 3840×2160→**2560×1440** (2×2 viewports, ~44% of the old area) — the bigger v1.2 world left too much dead space between spawns. Ship-relative spawn rings retuned to match: `SPAWN_MAX_DIST` 1100→**640**, `DOCK_MAX_DIST` 900→**620** (mins unchanged at 220/260), both now under the binding limit `min(WORLD_W,WORLD_H)/2−60 = 660` so a ring can never wrap around and land near-on-top of the ship. `STAR_DENSITY` untouched — `STAR_COUNT`'s area-derived formula auto-scales the far starfield layer to the smaller world, so visual density is preserved with no edit. Wrap/camera/render logic (`wrapPos`, `dist2`, `angleTo`, `shortDelta`, the camera transform) is correct against `WORLD_W/WORLD_H` symbolically and needed no changes (the `+120` wrap-jump discontinuity is a separate, pre-existing bug — v3.1 P2). Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-v31-world.js`, 12 assertions): constants at their new/clamped values and within the binding-limit clamp; many real `nextWave()` debris spawns and real `Dock` placements land within `[SPAWN_MIN_DIST, SPAWN_MAX_DIST]` / `[DOCK_MIN_DIST, DOCK_MAX_DIST]` of the ship; `STAR_COUNT` matches the area-derived formula for the new world size. Full regression (`test-f2`–`test-p6`, `test-boundary`, `test-starfield`, `test-firerate`, `test-targets`) re-run green. **P2: fix the wrap-jump discontinuity** — `wrap()` and `wrapNode()` (chain nodes) teleported by `WORLD_W + 120`/`WORLD_H + 120` while every distance/aim/render helper measures against period `WORLD_W`/`WORLD_H`; the undocumented +120 shifted every entity ~120 px relative to the ship at each seam crossing. Both jumps now teleport by exactly `WORLD_W`/`WORLD_H`; the ±60 px anti-flicker trigger margins are unchanged. Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-v31-wrap.js`, 14 assertions): `shortDelta` between an entity and a fixed partner stays continuous (no ~120 px jump) across a wrap on both axes and from both sides of each seam; a wrapped entity lands in `[0, WORLD_W)`/`[0, WORLD_H)`; a wrapped chain node's `px`/`py` shift by the same delta as `x`/`y` so implied velocity survives the teleport. Full regression (all 16 test files, 774 assertions) re-run green. See §2.11. **P3: garbage magnetism + coalescence → Hunter formation** — uncollected salvage is now a threat. Every `Garbage` gains a `coalesceDelay` (1 s activation) and a `pieces` count (both inherited by all emission sites + `Garbage.fromNode`); a new `coalesceGarbage(dt)` pass (run each frame after the pickup loop, before `updateChain`) makes **active** pieces (past their 1 s delay) mutually attract within `GARBAGE_MAGNET_RANGE` (140) at `GARBAGE_MAGNET_PULL` (40 px/s²), and two active pieces within `GARBAGE_MERGE_DIST` (12) **merge** — survivor takes the literal vector sum of both velocities and `pieces += other.pieces`, but **keeps its base mass** (FORK-2: a clump still tows as one mass-1.0 node). At `HUNTER_COALESCE_COUNT` (12) pieces the clump dies and spawns a `new HunterSatellite(x,y,3)` — **independent of `game.hunterTimer`**, so multiple concurrent lineages are allowed (FORK-1) — with a new ominous `AudioSys.hunterborn()` warning cue (two low descending sawtooth voices a dissonant tritone apart, ~0.4 s; audible even off-screen). Coalescing is a distinct fate: a merge sets `dead` **without** bumping `game.stats.garbageDecayed`, so it never trips Waste Not. New constants near `GARBAGE_DECAY` (incl. the off-by-default `GARBAGE_CLUMP_MAXSPD` = Infinity playtest clamp). Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-v31-coalesce.js`, 29 assertions): the 1 s gate on both attraction and merge (driven through the real `update()` countdown), a 2-piece merge with exact vector-sum velocity, twelve pieces → exactly one Hunter with `hunterborn` fired once, a wrap-seam merge, `garbageDecayed` untouched by a merge or a transform, a `pieces>1` clump hooking as a single mass-1.0 node through the real `update()`, and default-constructor/`fromNode`/emission-site inheritance. Full regression (all 18 test files, 815 assertions) re-run green. See §2.5.1/§2.7/§2.8.
- **v3.2 (shipped)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.2.md`, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.2.md`. **P1: garbage clumps become physical, and un-hookable** — reverses the v3.1 FORK-2 decision (which was only correct while clumps were hookable; P2 makes them un-hookable, removing FORK-2's reason). A `Garbage` clump's **`mass` now sums** on merge (a wad of 4 normal canisters is mass 4.0) and its **`radius` derives** as `7·√pieces` (a single piece still reads 7; an 11-clump ~23 px). The merge velocity switched from the literal vector sum to the **momentum sum** `(mₐvₐ + m_b v_b)/(mₐ+m_b)` (pre-merge masses) — with mass summing and garbage soon permanent, a literal sum made clumps the fastest things on screen; now a heavy clump barely speeds up eating a fast light piece. Attraction became **mass-weighted** and gravity-like (each piece accelerates toward the other ∝ the other's mass), momentum-conserving and reducing *exactly* to the shipped symmetric pull at mass 1.0 (so `GARBAGE_MAGNET_PULL` is unretuned) — heavy clumps become slow anchors loose singles fall into. `Garbage.draw()` renders a clump as a **cluster** of `pieces` mini-canisters at golden-angle offsets (`θ=k·2.39996`, `r=5·√k`) tumbling on `this.spin`; `pieces===1` is byte-identical to before. **A clump (`pieces>1`) cannot be hooked** (the pickup gate now requires `pieces===1`) and the **Magnet ignores it** — you must shoot it apart first (the shatter tool is P2, below). Clumps stay **non-solid** to the ship (FORK-A2: zero contact damage, not in `hazards`). No new constant (7 is the existing canister radius); decay/bullet-collision/emission untouched (later phases). Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-v31-coalesce.js` extended, **48 assertions** — the old exact-vector-sum assertion rewritten to the momentum sum): mass sums across a chain of merges, radius tracks `7·√pieces`, momentum-sum merge (a heavy clump absorbing a fast light piece barely speeds up), the mass-1.0 attraction reduction is bit-exact to the shipped force, a `pieces>1` clump is NOT hooked and the Magnet won't pull it while a single still hooks + is pulled, and `draw()` is crash-free at `pieces=1` and `pieces=11`. Full regression (all 18 test files, **834 assertions**) re-run green (`test-p5`/`test-p6` canister stubs gained `pieces:1` to match the new hook contract). See §2.5.1/§2.10. **P2: shatter a clump with one shot** — the tool that reopens what P1 made un-hookable. A new player-bullet-vs-garbage collision branch (in the non-hostile bullet loop, alongside the existing debris/saucer/hunter branches) targets ONLY `pieces > 1` clumps (tested against the P1-derived `radius`); a `pieces === 1` single is still not a bullet target and player bullets still pass straight through it, and hostile (saucer) bullets still pass through all garbage regardless of `pieces`. A hit calls the new flow function **`shatterClump(g)`** (shaped like `destroyDebris`/`destroyHunter`): `g.dead = true`, a small `boom()`, and exactly `g.pieces` fresh `new Garbage` singles pushed at `(g.x, g.y)`, each at `mass = g.mass / g.pieces` (per-piece mass identity is averaged back out — FLAG A-3, an accepted fidelity trade), `pieces = 1`, a **full, re-armed `coalesceDelay`** (the constructor default — reuses the P3-era constant, not a second one) so the burst disperses before it can re-clump, and an outward kick (new constant **`GARBAGE_SHATTER_KICK`**, `rand(40,90)` px/s) added to a fraction of the clump's own drift, mirroring the `destroyDebris` fan-out pattern. **No score** — the reward is the newly-hookable canisters. Decay, emission counts, the coalescence pass itself, and the Hunter transform are all untouched (P3 owns those). Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-v31-coalesce.js` extended, **61 assertions**, +13 over P1): one player bullet on a `pieces=7` clump yields exactly 7 live singles, all `pieces===1`, all with a full `coalesceDelay`, all `mass = clumpMass/7` (total mass conserved), and they do NOT re-merge on the very next frame (the delay gate holds, driven through the real `coalesceGarbage`/`update`); a player bullet passes THROUGH a `pieces=1` canister untouched; a hostile bullet passes through a clump untouched; the emitted singles ARE hookable (the P1 gate now lets them through) via two real `update()` frames; shattering leaves the Waste-Not stat unchanged. Full regression (all 18 test files, **847 assertions**) re-run green. See §2.5.1/§2.10. **P3: salvage is permanent; the garbage economy closes** — garbage **no longer decays**. The `decay` field, the `GARBAGE_DECAY`/`GARBAGE_SEVER_DECAY` constants, the decay countdown/death in `Garbage.update`, the blink-out branch in `Garbage.draw`, and the `garbageDecayed` stat are all **removed**; a canister now leaves the field by exactly two doors — **recycled** or **consumed into a Hunter**. This *supersedes* GDD §2.10.1's shipped "decay exists to protect readability — don't remove it" rationale, which is rewritten in place (with the reason it was superseded, so a future session doesn't "restore" it): coalescence + shatter-to-harvest are now the density levers. **FORK-B / B1 closes the loop:** a coalescence-born core is tagged **`bornOfScrap`**, propagated to its split children in `destroyHunter`, and a `bornOfScrap` Hunter emits **NO** garbage at any tier — because without this, a scrap-born lineage would drop `12 + 54 = 66` canisters (a 5.5× amplifier: 12 pieces in → 66 out), and with permanent garbage that diverges. Now it's **12 in, 0 out**; score, splits, damage, and the small-tier powerup drop are all unchanged. Timer-spawned Hunters are untouched and still drop the full 66. Two constants retuned (both playtest knobs): **`GARBAGE_COALESCE_DELAY` 1.0→6.0 s** (same-explosion siblings now drift 120–330 px apart and *happen upon* strangers instead of instantly re-clumping) and **`GARBAGE_MAGNET_RANGE` 140→260** (140 was tuned for 12-second garbage; permanent garbage that drifts further apart would never re-find anything — FLAG D-1, the number most likely to need tuning). The **Waste Not** achievement is repurposed in place (id + pool slot kept, so the weekly-rotation math and `test-f9` slice assertions are unchanged): its old "zero canisters expired" test auto-unlocked every game once decay was gone, so it now reads "finish a game with **no Hunters born from neglected scrap**" (`s.hunterCoalesced === 0`), driven by a new per-game `game.stats.hunterCoalesced` incremented once at the coalescence transform site. Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-v31-coalesce.js` extended to **80 assertions**; `test-f9.js` to **283**; `test-f3.js` adjusted for the dropped ctor decay param): a canister survives a ~120 s `update()` run and never dies of age; a `bornOfScrap` core killed through its FULL lineage (large → 3 med → 9 small) emits **zero** garbage while awarding the **same** score and still dropping its small-tier powerup; a timer-spawned lineage still emits the full 12 normal + 54 low; the `bornOfScrap` flag survives both split generations; `hunterCoalesced` increments once per transform; Waste Not unlocks on a zero-coalescence game and does **not** after one Hunter is born from scrap; the weekly pool is still length 16 with every `poolIndex` assertion unchanged. Full regression (all 18 test files, **872 assertions**) re-run green. See §2.5.1/§2.10/§2.10.1/§2.17.
- **v3.6 (Phase 1 of N)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.6.md` §2/§3/§4, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.6.md` Phase 1. Presentation: garbage colour, wraparound-boundary removal, scoop scale + a translucent capture box. Render/constants only — no sim, collision, or pickup logic touched. **PART A — all garbage glows one safe green (FORK-1 = Option B).** `COLOR.clumpHot` (`#ff5a2a`, the red proximity-to-Hunter lerp) is **deleted**. `Garbage.draw()`'s `pieces === 1` and `pieces > 1` branches now pick colour by the identical rule — per-piece mass `this.mass / this.pieces < 1 ? COLOR.garbageLight : COLOR.garbage` — where before a clump ignored its own mass and only read the red lerp. The chain-node render (`n.mass < 1 ? garbageLight : garbage`) was already this rule and stays byte-identical. `lerpColor()` had no other caller and is deleted alongside it; the stale `clumpHot` mention in `COLOR.lowhp`'s comment is fixed. **What's genuinely lost:** the clump's proximity-to-Hunter tell — size (`radius = 7·√pieces`) is now the only signal, a real but much quieter one. Deliberate trade, not an oversight (§2.5.1 records why). **PART B — the wraparound-boundary overlay is deleted outright.** `drawWorldBoundary()`, its call site in `draw()`, and the four `BOUNDARY_*` constants (`BOUNDARY_DASH/GAP/WIDTH/GLOW`) are gone; `scratchpad/test-boundary.js` (20 assertions, entirely about the boundary) is deleted rather than repaired. No replacement overlay — whether wrap reads fine without an explanatory guide is now a playtest question. **PART C — the scoop mouth grows and becomes visible.** `SCOOP_CONFIG.maxWidthMult` 3.0→**5.0** (L5 mouth 54px→90px) and `maxDepth` 36→**60** (both commented as playtest starting points, not settled — Paul re-picks them in `tools/scoop-lab.html`); `buildScoopSteps`, index 0, and the load-time `SCOOP_WIDTH[0] !== 0` throw are untouched, so the `scoopLevel === 0` byte-identical invariant holds by construction. `Ship.draw()`'s scoop render — previously an open `drawPoly` V (`[[d,-hw],[16,0],[d,hw]]`) that was never the actual capture region — is replaced by the **exact box** `inScoopBox()` tests: corners `[[-SHIP_RADIUS,-hw],[d,-hw],[d,hw],[-SHIP_RADIUS,hw]]`, every value derived from `SCOOP_WIDTH`/`SCOOP_DEPTH`/`SHIP_RADIUS` (never hardcoded), drawn as a translucent fill (`COLOR.dock`, alpha 0.15, a look-call knob) with the usual `glowStroke` outline on top — before the hull, inside the `!blink` block, hidden at level 0. This is a deliberate, code-commented exception to §3.2's no-fills rule (§3.2 updated to record it). `tools/scoop-lab.html` updated in the same commit — its verbatim duplicate prong-V draw replaced by the same box logic, so the lab previews what the game actually captures. **Tests:** extended `scratchpad/test-v33-p1.js` §6 (no `clumpHot` anywhere in the source; a clump's drawn colour matches its per-piece mass at `pieces` 2/5/11, both above and below the mass-1 threshold) and `scratchpad/test-v33-p3.js` (no `drawWorldBoundary`/`BOUNDARY_*` in the source; `SCOOP_WIDTH[5] === 5 * SHIP_DRAW_W` exactly; `SCOOP_WIDTH[0] === 0 && SCOOP_DEPTH[0] === 0` still holds; and — the load-bearing check — **the drawn box's four corners, recovered from a recording ctx via a real `Ship.draw()` call, agree with `inScoopBox`'s accept/reject boundary at levels 1..5**, probing just inside/outside each of the front, rear (`-SHIP_RADIUS`), and both lateral edges). One pre-existing hardcoded assertion in `test-v33-p3.js` §3 (lateral 40 vs. the old 27px L5 half-width) was rewritten relative to the new `SCOOP_WIDTH[5]`, since 40 is now legitimately inside the wider mouth — not a regression, the old literal was just stale. `scratchpad/test-v34-p5.js` §A's `COLOR.lowhp` distinctness check against the now-deleted `COLOR.clumpHot` was dropped (that constant no longer exists to be distinct from). Full regression re-run green: **all 23 test files (`test-boundary.js` deleted), 1621 assertions**. `node --check` clean on both the extracted main-build script and `tools/scoop-lab.html`. GDD updated in place: **§2.5.1** (the Cluster-render bullet superseded a third time — the red lerp's removal, and what's lost), **§2.14.1** (the new `SCOOP_CONFIG` numbers, the box render replacing the prong-V), **§3.2** (the one documented fills exception), the world-boundary bullet (marked removed, history preserved), the Architecture Map (Constants / Entity classes / draw() rows), the top Version line, and this entry. Did NOT push.

- **v3.6 (Phase 2 of N)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.6.md` §7/§8, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.6.md` Phase 2. Feel pass, two independent parts. **PART A — the Magnet buff.** The culprit was `MAGNET_DAMP` (0.06), not `MAGNET_PULL`: at 0.06 it stripped ~4.6% of a piece's velocity every frame, turning the pull into a low terminal-velocity governor (`v_terminal ≈ accel/2.7`) rather than an acceleration — combined with the hardcoded quadratic falloff, a piece 190px out only felt ~175 px/s² and topped out near 65 px/s. Three constants, all playtest knobs: the falloff exponent hoisted out of the inline `t*t` into `MAGNET_FALLOFF_POW` (shipped **1.0**, linear); `MAGNET_PULL_MIN` **60→150** (the far-field floor); `MAGNET_DAMP` **0.06→0.35** (counter-intuitively *less* damping — the biggest single lever, and the riskiest for overshoot/orbiting). `MAGNET_RANGE` (380) and the `accel /= √mass` scaling are untouched. **PART B — large-Hunter last-stand pursuit.** A large Hunter core (`size === 3`) still tumbles unconditionally, but once `game.debris.length === 0 && !game.ship.dead` it now also steers its heading toward the ship (wrap-aware `angleTo` + shortest-angular-delta turn) at new constants `HUNTER_LAST_STAND_SPEED` (50 px/s) and `HUNTER_LAST_STAND_TURN` (0.5 rad/s) — both deliberately below even a wave-1 medium homer, so a wave can no longer stall on an un-huntable drifting core once it's the only satellite left, without giving the core a new silhouette (FLAG-G: legibility is playtest-only). GDD updated in place: **§2.14** (Magnet numbers), **§2.5** (Hunter last-stand behavior), the top Version line, and this entry. Two commits (P2a, P2b). Did NOT push.

- **v3.6 (Phase 3 of N)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.6.md` §5, CONFLICT-3/CONFLICT-4, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.6.md` Phase 3. **The powerup drop economy replaced: three deterministic sources instead of a 16%-per-small-tier-kill chance roll.** `POWERUP_DROP_CHANCE` and both `maybeDropPowerup()` call sites (`destroyDebris`'s and `destroyHunter`'s small-tier branches) are deleted — Debris now drops nothing, ever, and neither do small/medium Hunters. `maybeDropPowerup` is reworked into an unconditional `dropPowerup(x, y, vx, vy)`: still rolls the unchanged `POWERUP_DROP_WEIGHTS` table (`scoop` still deliberately absent from `POWERUP_DROP_TYPES`, the timed-effect list — Constraint 2 verified unaffected), but the chance gate is gone; callers decide **when**, this only decides **what**. Three call sites replace the old roll: **(1) every Saucer kill**, large or small — a new `destroySaucer(s)` flow function (shaped like `destroyDebris`/`destroyHunter`) is extracted as the choke point for the two previously copy-pasted kill sites (player-bullet branch, shield-body-contact branch), removing that duplication hazard; the drop inherits the saucer's `vx, vy` exactly, no scaling. **(2) every large Hunter core** (`h.size === 3` only, not its medium/small children), inheriting `h.vx, h.vy`. **(3) the recycle hub**, latched on `game.deliveryCount === 10` (one line above the existing `=== 12` Heavy Hauler latch, same "exactly once per visit" idiom) — emits one powerup from the dock's own position at a new `DOCK_POWERUP_SPEED` (120 px/s, playtest knob) in a random direction, plus a "SALVAGE BONUS" `FloatText` at the dock. Also deleted the settling drag in `Powerup.update()` (`vx *= Math.pow(0.4, dt)`) — a drop now flies its full launch vector until collected, expired, or wrapped; byte-identical for ambient Health, which still spawns at rest via the untouched `spawnHealthPowerup()`/`POWERUP_HEALTH_GAP` timer. **A deliberate, flagged economy shift (CONFLICT-3):** field supply moves from "any small-tier kill, 16% of the time" (Debris was the most common target in the game) to "every UFO + one per full Hunter lineage + one per 10 canisters delivered" — early waves with few Hunters and sparse saucers could run drier than before; flagged for playtest, not blocked. **Tests:** extended `scratchpad/test-v33-p3.js` (owns the drop economy — constants, the weighted roll, a full 13-kill Debris lineage drops zero, a full 13-kill Hunter lineage drops exactly one from the large core, both saucer-kill paths each drop exactly one on the saucer's own vector with matching score/achievement counters as a regression guard on the `destroySaucer` extraction, and the drag-removal speed-retention check) and `scratchpad/test-p6.js` (owns dock offload — the hub's per-visit latch: 9 canisters emits none, 10 emits exactly one from the dock's position at `DOCK_POWERUP_SPEED`, an 11th/12th in the same visit emits no more). Also fixed three now-stale regression tests that referenced the removed `maybeDropPowerup`/`POWERUP_DROP_CHANCE` identifiers directly in their `new Function` return lists: `test-f6.js`'s old small-tier-drop section is trimmed to the one invariant that still holds (Health never in the drop pool) and now defers to `test-v33-p3.js`; `test-v31-coalesce.js`'s scrap-born-lineage check updated its expected powerup count from 9 (one per small kill) to 1 (the large core only). Full regression re-run green: **all 22 test files**. `node --check` clean on the extracted script. GDD updated in place: **§2.14** (Spawn sources, Pickup/lifecycle, the constants callout), **§2.10** (the Recycling dock bullet gains the hub-emission cross-reference), the Architecture Map (Flow-functions row), the top Version line, and this entry. Did NOT push.
- **v3.6 (Phase 4 of N)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.6.md` §6, FORK-3, CONFLICT-5, CONFLICT-6, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.6.md` Phase 4. Two independent parts. **PART A — powerup stacking banks (FORK-3 resolved yes).** `applyPowerup()`'s two same-type-pickup assignments (`game.powerFx[type] = powerDuration(type)`, `game.powerBudget[type] = POWERUP_BUDGET[type]`) become `+=` — a same-type pickup now **adds** to what's left instead of resetting to full, reversing the v1.7/v3.0-P5 "refresh, never add" rule. **Magnitude still never stacks** — two Rapids don't double the fire rate, only duration/shot-count accumulate. The HUD's `frac` was already `clamp01`'d, so a banked surplus needed no other change: a full bar just means "at least one pickup's worth left," surplus invisible — the accepted behaviour, per spec. **PART B — the HUD rebuilt.** `drawHUD()`'s left column is rebuilt top-to-bottom as **Score / Level / Hull / Shield / Cargo / Powerups remaining**, with row y-offsets hoisted into a local `row` layout cursor (previously six bare literals). The **`TARGETS` readout and `targetsLeft` are deleted** (the wave-clear gate `debris.length === 0 && hunters.length === 0` is untouched — only the display died) along with `scratchpad/test-targets.js` (all 12 of its assertions were about the readout). The **shield bar moves out of the top-right corner** (`bx = VIEW_W − 30 − bw`) into the left column directly beneath Hull, same bar geometry. Hull, Shield and Cargo now render their labels and nominal fills in `COLOR.text` — the same colour as the score — with the existing alarm-state overrides kept (Hull red below 30%, Shield red below 25%; Cargo `COLOR.dim` when empty, was `COLOR.garbage` when hauling). **Hull at max is now unmistakable:** at `hp === SHIP_MAX_HP` the bar fills gold (`COLOR.ach`) with a `MAX` tag beside it, since a Health pickup at that point would be wasted and the player needs to see that at a glance. **Powerups remaining:** a time-limited row (`powerMode(t) === "time"`) keeps its bar unchanged; a **count-limited row draws no bar at all** — banking removed any meaningful ceiling to draw one against — just the glyph and the plain remaining number. The **SCOOP pip row is kept**, unmoved, directly under the powerup rows (persistent state, deliberately outside the `POWERUP_DROP_TYPES` loop). **Tests:** extended `scratchpad/test-p5.js` (owns powerup expiry modes + the HUD bar; drives the real `draw()` through a recording canvas measuring bar-fill pixel widths) with a new section (L) — no `TARGETS` text anywhere in a plain draw; the `SHIELD` label's recorded x sits in the left column; the hull bar's recorded `fillStyle` is `COLOR.ach` at exactly max HP and `COLOR.text` one HP below max, with/without a `MAX` tag respectively; a count-mode Rapid row draws its remaining-shots number but no bar rect; a time-mode Rapid row still draws its bar — plus extended section (H) to assert two same-type pickups bank (budget/timer additive, not clamped to one pickup's worth) while fire cadence after two Rapids equals after one (magnitude never stacks). Also fixed `scratchpad/test-f6.js` §D, which encoded the old refresh assumption directly (`same-type pickup REFRESHES to POWERUP_DURATION`) — rewritten to assert the banked sum. Full regression re-run: **all 21 files** (`test-targets.js` gone, not failing), **1533 assertions**, all green. `node --check` clean on the extracted script. - **v3.6 (Phase 5 of N)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.6.md` §9, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.6.md` Phase 5. **Game over is a spectacle: a new `dying` state between `playing` and `gameover`.** `killShip()` now sets `game.state = "dying"` (and arms `game.deathT = DEATH_DURATION` 2.5 s + `game.shake`) instead of jumping straight to `gameover` — but everything else it did is **unchanged and still fires at `killShip`**: the `boom`/`scatterChain`, the `thrust`/`lowhp`/`saucer` teardowns, and the whole achievement flush (`game.stats.gameEnded = true` + `Achievements.evaluate()` + `Achievements.save()`), so achievement timing is byte-identical. A new **`updateDeath(dt)`** runs before `update()`'s `state !== "playing"` early-return: it advances particles/floaters/garbage/debris/hunters/saucers/powerups + the camera and filters dead entities, but runs **no** ship input, spawns, pickups, collisions, wave-clear, heartbeat, or `Achievements.evaluate`. **The spectacle** (all new playtest-knob constants): an expanding **shockwave ring** (`DEATH_SHOCKWAVE_SPEED` 700 px/s) is the detonation front — any Debris/Hunter it reaches detonates via `destroyDebris(a, false)` / `destroyHunter(h, false)`, nearest-first falling out for free; **screen shake** (`DEATH_SHAKE_INIT`/`DEATH_SHAKE_DECAY`, added to the camera translate); and a **white flash** (`DEATH_FLASH_TIME`/`DEATH_FLASH_ALPHA`, a full-viewport `fillRect` after the world). At `deathT ≤ 0` → `gameover` (a clean seam for Phase 6's high-score flow). Music: `dying` falls through `musicStateFor()` to `"off"`, so `MUSIC_FADE_OUT` runs under the explosion. **The `awardScore = false` detonations move no score AND no achievement counters** — but `destroyHunter` had incremented `hunterLineageKills`/`largeHunterKills`/lifetime `hunterKills` *unconditionally* (unlike `destroyDebris`, which already gated its counters), so those three were **moved inside `if (awardScore)`** to match; both real gameplay callers pass `true`, so live play is unchanged (this also closes a latent lifetime-`hunterKills` leak the previously-unused `awardScore=false` path would have had). **All `game.state` read sites audited** (confirm→`startGame` correctly excluded so the spectacle can't be skipped or restarted; pause / `o`-menu / gamepad `onTitleOrOver` excluded; `AudioSys.thrust` silent; HUD low-health pointer hidden; menu/`rootItems` unreachable; `musicStateFor` → `"off"`). **FLAG-I resolved: `Capture`'s `P` screenshot IS allowed during `dying`** (a new `Capture.canShoot()` — plausibly the frame most worth capturing) while `O` slow-mo / `H` HUD-toggle stay live-play only. **Tests:** new `scratchpad/test-v36-death.js` (45 assertions) drives the real `killShip`/`update`/`draw`: `killShip` enters `dying` not `gameover` and fires `gameEnded`+`evaluate`+`save` exactly once (spied) at `killShip`, not at the later transition; the field genuinely keeps moving during `dying`; score and every achievement counter stay put through a window where nearby bodies really detonate; after `DEATH_DURATION` the state is exactly `gameover`; a confirm keypress during `dying` does not start a game (and still does at `gameover`); `draw()` is crash-free through the window; plus the `P`-during-`dying` / no-`O` / no-`P`-at-`gameover` Capture behaviour. `scratchpad/test-f2.js` §d updated (a lethal hit now enters `dying`, settling to `gameover` after the window). Full regression re-run green: **all 23 test files, 1727 assertions**. `node --check` clean. - **v3.5 (the final music track set + the intensity freeze)** — the `title`/`tense`/`retro`/`ambient` builders (v3.4 P6/P7) were **deleted** and replaced by the five tracks composed and auditioned in `tools/music-lab.html`'s PORT-ME BLOCK B, **ported verbatim** (no re-composition, no re-tuning of a single gain): `buildBeaconTitle` (title — C major, a Lydian ♯4 departure lift, ~21.8 s), `buildZenTrack` (the calm **default** — the old title arc at 0.25 s resolution + subdued percussion, 48 s), `buildDerelictTrack` (chromatic-mediant pads, no beat, 24 s), `buildDriftTrack` (organ-pulse hymn, ~21.8 s), and `buildWarehouseTrack` (house — kick/16th-hat/two 7th-chord stabs, no melodic hook, 23 s). BLOCK B's `mk`/`put`/`hit` step helpers came along (they back all five builders — the orphaned `mkSteps`/`putStep` from P7 were dropped); nothing else was ported (BLOCK A's four `playNote` extensions landed in v3.5 P1; everything below BLOCK B is lab UI). `MUSIC_TRACKS` re-keyed to `{title, zen, derelict, drift, warehouse, off}`; `MUSIC_TRACK_VALUES = ["zen","derelict","drift","warehouse"]` (calm→hot), `MUSIC_TRACK_LABELS` updated, `settings.musicTrack` default `"retro"`→**`"zen"`**. **THE FREEZE — the load-bearing decision:** no track carries a `tier` field, so every `setState()` gate is built at `(layer.tier || 1) === 1` (always on) and `setIntensity()` (which opens `if (lg.tier === 1) continue;`) walks the gate list and does nothing — the v3.4-P7 difficulty-gated intensity layering goes **DORMANT with no code change at all**. `musicStateFor()`, `STORAGE_KEY`, the menu row layout, `MUSIC_LAYER_THRESHOLD`, `MUSIC_LAYER_CROSSFADE`, `setIntensity()`, `layerGates`, and the `setIntensity()` call site in `nextWave()` were all deliberately **left in place** — re-arming the machinery later means adding `tier` fields back to track data and nothing else (the composed tiers 2-4 were auditioned and rejected). **Persistence consequence (expected, not a bug):** `loadSettings` accepts `musicTrack` only if it's in `MUSIC_TRACK_VALUES`, so a save holding `"retro"`/`"tense"`/`"ambient"` is now rejected and falls back to `"zen"` — no crash, no key rename, `afd_settings_v1` stays frozen. Headless-tested: extended `scratchpad/test-v34-p6.js` in place (the music-system owner — 152→**233** assertions) — driving the REAL `MusicSys`/`nextWave`/`musicStateFor`/`loadSettings`/menu, no reimplementation. Its old-track sections were retargeted to the new set and semantics: **(a)** every track loop ≥ 10 s; **(b)** no gap longer than **one** step where nothing across any layer is sounding (checked circularly — a single-step rest, e.g. a 16th rest in Warehouse's groove, is music; the old ambient bug was multi-second holes; measured longest silent run: Warehouse 1, all others 0); **(c) the freeze** — no layer in any track carries a `tier` field, every gate builds tier 1, and a full 0→1→0 `setIntensity` sweep ramps **no** gate and never changes the audible-layer count; **(d)** worst-case node creation for a single scheduled step across all five tracks is **13** (`zen` step 0: bass+padLo+padMid+kick), asserted ≤ 16; **(e)** a fresh instance loading a save with `musicTrack:"retro"` (also `"tense"`/`"ambient"`) comes up `"zen"` while its other valid fields load normally; **(f)** the four-value picker cycles and wraps in both directions. The `playNote`-field-wiring section (noise/hp/drop/cutoffTo/q) was kept but its old "no shipped layer uses these" inertness assertion inverted — the new tracks genuinely exercise those branches. Full regression re-run green: **all 24 test files, 1588 assertions** (up from 1507 — only `test-v34-p6.js` changed, +81; no other file touched). `node --check` clean on the extracted script.
