- **v3.5 (Phase 3 of N)** — the low-health warning is a pulsed, HP-scaled alarm. **The problem (verified by grep before editing):** `AudioSys.lowhp(on)` was a 220 Hz sine, FM-warbled ±18 Hz by a 0.6 Hz LFO, at a **constant** gain of 0.05 — the quietest voice on the SFX bus (peers: explosion 0.5, hit 0.16, fire 0.12, thrust 0.10 continuous, saucer 0.055 continuous), a pure sine with no harmonics to cut through anything, and constant-amplitude — the ear adapts away a steady tone, so it got *less* audible the longer it played. Raising the gain alone would have made it more annoying and no more noticeable; the fix had to change the voice's **shape**, not just its volume. **The rebuild** keeps the exact persistent-voice idiom of `thrust(on)`/`saucer(on)` (stored nodes built on `true`, torn down on `false`): a root sine oscillator (`LOWHP_ROOT_FREQ`, unchanged 220 Hz) plus a soft harmonic partner a fifth above (`LOWHP_HARMONIC_RATIO` 1.5, at `LOWHP_HARMONIC_GAIN_FRAC` 0.35 of the root's level — a body, so it reads as an instrument panel, not a test tone, and survives an explosion), both summed into a shared **amplitude-LFO "pulse" gain node** (an `lfo` oscillator → `lfoGain` → the pulse gain's `.gain`, DC-offset by `LOWHP_PULSE_DEPTH`) — a slow cockpit-warning **beep**, not a drone: onsets get noticed, the gaps in between keep it bearable over a long low-HP stretch. Base gain raised into `thrust`'s neighborhood (`LOWHP_GAIN_MIN` 0.08 → `LOWHP_GAIN_MAX` 0.13) — modest, since the pulsing does most of the perceptual work. **HP-scaled urgency (FORK-3, resolved HP-scaled):** a new `AudioSys.lowhpSet(t)` — a no-op if the voice isn't live or `ctx` is null — sets the pulse LFO's rate (`LOWHP_PULSE_RATE_MIN` 0.9 Hz → `LOWHP_PULSE_RATE_MAX` 2.4 Hz) and the root/harmonic gain from urgency `t = 1 − hp/LOW_HP_THRESHOLD` (0 at the threshold, ~1 near death) — a gentle "hey" at 100 HP, a real alarm at 20. Called **every frame** (not edge-detected) from the ONE existing edge-detect site in `update()`, right after camera-follow, alongside the pre-existing `lowhp(true)`/`(false)` calls — that site only runs while playing-and-unpaused, and `killShip`/`quitToTitle`/`openPause`/`startGame` already tear the voice down, so no new teardown site or game state was needed. Params move via `linearRampToValueAtTime` over `LOWHP_PARAM_RAMP` (0.15 s, same idiom as `MusicSys.setDuck`/`setIntensity`) — never a bare per-frame `.value` set, which would zipper — and `lowhpSet` is idempotent on `t` (a steady-HP frame reschedules nothing). All new numbers are named playtest knobs (§2.8). **Out of scope, both logged as flags, not built:** FLAG-8a (v3.4 P5, still open, now sharper — see §2.12) and a synced red vignette pulse (FLAG-3b, still just an idea). Headless-tested: extended `scratchpad/test-v34-p5.js` in place (33→**74** assertions, +41) — the four pre-existing teardown assertions (§D) pass unchanged against the rebuilt voice (the load-bearing regression guard against a leaked droning oscillator); the rising/falling edge still fires `lowhp(true)`/`(false)` exactly once; the voice builds its pulse LFO + harmonic partner without throwing and nulls every stored handle (`lowhpOsc`/`lowhpGain`/`lowhpT`) on teardown; `lowhpSet` — urgency ~0 at the threshold and ~1 near death, pulse rate/gain monotonically non-decreasing as HP falls, every move is a `linearRampToValueAtTime` (never a bare set), idempotent on repeated `t`, and a safe no-op with no live voice / `ctx === null`; a real 120-frame `update()` run at fixed low HP proves the per-frame `lowhpSet` call never rebuilds the node graph (checked via object-identity snapshots of the oscillator/gain nodes, not a global oscillator-creation counter — the heartbeat/wave-clear/saucer-spawn subsystems legitimately create their own oscillators during a real `update()` run, which would have made a global counter flaky). Full regression re-run green: **all 24 test files, 1507 assertions** (up from 1466 — only `test-v34-p5.js` changed; every other file untouched). `node --check` clean on the extracted script. `test-p5` §G and `test-boundary` §E (documented pre-existing RNG flakes) stayed green across 15 isolated re-runs each — no new flake. Did NOT push. See §2.8/§2.12.
- **v3.5 (Phase 2 of N)** — a garbage clump now renders as a larger canister, not an asteroid. **The problem:** a clump (`pieces > 1`) drew as a 7–9 vertex jittered hull polygon (`makeClumpHull`, v3.3 P1), whose explicit design intent was "reads as a target, not a pile of pickups" — a rationale written while clumps were **un-hookable** (v3.2 P1's rule at the time). v3.3 P4 (9c) reversed that premise: it made a clump directly **scoopable** (flying into the capture region banks as many pieces as the chain can hold), but the art never caught up — players kept reading the hazard-shaped hull as a thing to avoid, not fly into. **The fix:** `drawCanister(x, y, angle, alpha, color, scale = 1)` gained a trailing `scale` param that scales both the body poly and the hazard stripe; the two pre-existing call sites (the single-canister branch in `Garbage.draw()` and the chain-node render loop) omit the arg and are byte-identical to before (the load-bearing regression guard). `Garbage.draw()`'s `pieces > 1` branch now draws exactly ONE `drawCanister` at `scale = this.radius / 7` (`= √pieces`, since `radius = 7·√pieces`) — no new constant — so the drawn long half-axis exactly equals the collision radius by construction. The `lerpColor(COLOR.garbage → COLOR.clumpHot)` danger tint (scaled by `pieces / HUNTER_COALESCE_COUNT`) is kept as the only tell a clump is nearing the Hunter transform; the radioactive alpha flicker comes free from `drawCanister`. **`this.hull` and `makeClumpHull` are deleted entirely** — all three sites that held or regenerated the field (the `Garbage` constructor, the merge in `coalesceGarbage`, and the partial-scoop leftover re-derivation in the pickup pass) simply drop it, not just stop reading it. Untouched: `this.radius` (`7·√pieces`) and all collision math, the bullet-vs-clump shatter branch, `coalesceGarbage`'s merge math, the scoop capture geometry, and the `pieces === 1` single render. **Tests** — rewrote `scratchpad/test-v33-p1.js` in place (the file that owns the clump render): its old cached-hull assertions (stable across frames, regenerates at merge) are replaced with their inverse (no `hull` field on a fresh `Garbage`, after a real `coalesceGarbage` merge, or on a real partial-scoop leftover driven through `update()`; `makeClumpHull` absent from the source), plus a new extent check (a recording ctx capturing `moveTo`/`lineTo` args confirms the drawn body/stripe extent at `pieces = 2/5/11` tracks `this.radius` exactly) and a default-scale check (`drawCanister` with no trailing arg draws at the unscaled ±7 extent — the two untouched call sites' regression guard). Also fixed the two hull assertions surviving in `scratchpad/test-v31-coalesce.js`'s partial-scoop test (#23) in place, asserting no `hull` field instead of hull-regeneration. Full regression re-run green: **all 24 test files, 1466 assertions**. GDD updated in place: **§2.5.1** (the Cluster-render rationale rewritten with the supersession history, and the Scoopable bullet's stale "cached hull regenerated" mention removed), the Architecture Map (**Constants** and **Entity classes** rows), the top Version line, and this entry. Did NOT push.
- **v3.5 (Phase 1 of N)** — a bugfix session (not a `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.5.md` phase — two independently reported/confirmed causes behind "switching the Options Music Track mid-game sounds like the music stopped"). **PART A — the keyboard menu handler had no `e.repeat` guard.** The `keydown` listener's menu-open branch (`if (menuActive())`) called `handleMenuKey(k)` on every event, including browser key **auto-repeat** (~30/s while a key is held) — the gamepad path (`handleGamepadMenu` → `menuNavEdges()`) was already strictly edge-detected, but keyboard wasn't. On the 3-value Music Track row, a brief hold could spin the selection back to where it started ("nothing changed" from the player's view) while re-entering `MusicSys.setState()` nearly every frame — each call discarding and rebuilding `trackGain` and restarting its 0.6 s crossfade ramp from `0.0001`, pinning the music near-silent for as long as the key was held. **Fix:** the menu-open branch now returns early on `e.repeat` (`preventDefault()` still fires, so the key doesn't scroll the page); the rebind-capture and normal-play branches are untouched. **Flagged consequence (not a bug):** the three volume sliders and the two Difficulty toggles are driven by the same branch, so a held key no longer scrubs them either — a full 1.0→0.0 volume sweep is now 10 taps, matching gamepad feel. No throttled-repeat softening was added; that's a possible playtest follow-up. **PART B — `ambient`'s tier-1 foundation was inaudible, not just "calm."** `buildAmbientTrack()`'s always-on tier-1 layer carried exactly one note per 8 s loop (sine, gain 0.06) — since tiers 2-4 don't unlock until wave 3+ (`MUSIC_LAYER_THRESHOLD`), tier-1 is the *entire* audible track at wave 1, and measured against the real scheduler over a 10 s window it produced 9 scheduled notes vs. retro's 127 and tense's 138 — roughly 25× thinner, which is what actually made Ambient sound like silence rather than a deliberately mellow track. **Fix (layer-data only — the scheduler, `setState`/`setIntensity`, `MUSIC_TRACKS`, `musicStateFor`, `MUSIC_LAYER_THRESHOLD`, and the title/tense/retro tracks are all untouched):** the foundation layer is now two overlapping root/fifth (E2/B2) pad swells offset every 2 s across the 8 s loop, each one's release overlapping the next one's attack, so the layer is **continuously present** with no silent gap anywhere in the loop; its gain went 0.06→**0.075**, in family with retro's/tense's 0.075/0.08 bass (the other three tiers were nudged up the same way — pulse/harmony/lead 0.035/0.04/0.03 → 0.045/0.05/0.045). Key (E dorian), tempo, character (slow, sparse, "long haul in the dark"), and the 4-tier gate structure are all unchanged — Ambient is now the **calmest** track, not the **quietest**. **Tests** — extended `scratchpad/test-v34-p6.js` in place (the file that owns the music system), new sections **O/P, +12 assertions (140→152)**, driving the REAL `keydown` listener(s)/`MusicSys`/`MUSIC_TRACKS` — no reimplementation: (O) a real keydown with `repeat:true` on the Music Track row, a volume slider row, and a Difficulty toggle row each leaves the setting unchanged, while a `repeat:false` keydown on each moves it exactly once; a repeat keydown during **normal play** (no menu open) still writes into `keys{}`, proving the guard didn't leak into gameplay. (P) a density-based regression guard (notes/sec, not raw count, since Ambient's loop tempo is deliberately ~4-8× slower than its siblings) asserts Ambient's tier-1-only density is within 1/25th of retro's and tense's (chosen loose — a guard against near-zero presence, not a precision target) and that its tier-1 notes span at least half the loop rather than clustering in one step (the shape of the original bug). Full regression re-run green: **all 24 test files, 1456 assertions** (up from 1444 — only `test-v34-p6.js` changed, +12). `node --check` clean on the extracted script. GDD updated in place: **§2.8** (Ambient's rebuilt layer data + the measured density parity), **§2.16** (the keyboard repeat guard + the volume/Difficulty-toggle consequence), the Architecture Map (**Input** row, **MusicSys** row label), the top Version line, and this entry. Did NOT push.
- **v3.4 (Phase 7 of N)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.4.md` §9b/§9c, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.4.md`. **P7: the three gameplay music tracks + difficulty-gated intensity layers.** Builds on P6's `MusicSys` scheduler — no scheduler changes, only DATA. **(1) THREE TRACKS, all step-sequencer data:** `tense` (D minor, 120bpm 16th-note bass through a tight lowpass — "insistent"), `retro` (A major, square/saw, bright — the vector-arcade lineage, closest to `drawPoly`+`glowStroke`/CRT-palette/synthesized-SFX, so it ships as the **default**, FORK-9 confirmed), `ambient` (E dorian, slow sparse pads — the "long haul in the dark" salvage-sim mood). Each built by its own `buildXTrack()` (`buildTenseTrack`/`buildRetroTrack`/`buildAmbientTrack`), sharing new top-level `mkSteps`/`putStep` helpers (the title track keeps its own local `mk`/`put` — untouched, lower risk than refactoring P6-tested code). Registered into `MUSIC_TRACKS` **by name** (`tense`/`retro`/`ambient`), replacing the old `play: null` stub — this is what lets `musicStateFor()` (below) route a track switch through `setState()`'s existing crossfade with zero new code. **(2) INTENSITY LAYERS — the layer thickens the SAME loop, it never swaps.** Each gameplay track's 4 layers carry a `tier` field (1 foundation / 2 pulse / 3 harmony / 4 lead; an absent tier defaults to 1 — why the title track's untiered layers are unaffected and stay always-on). New `MUSIC_LAYER_THRESHOLD = {2: 0.20, 3: 0.45, 4: 0.70}` gates directly off the **shipped** `difficultyFactor(game.wave)` curve — no second curve invented, per the prompt. **Architecturally, gating is a downstream GAIN GATE, not a scheduling omission**: `MusicSys.setState` now builds one persistent `GainNode` per layer (`this.layerGates`, `[{node, tier, target}]`), inserted between each note's envelope gain and `trackGain`; `scheduleStep`/`playNote` schedule **every** layer unconditionally on every step regardless of intensity — only the gate's own gain value determines audibility. This is the load-bearing design choice that makes "tempo/key identical across intensity" true **by construction**, not by a parallel invariant that could drift: there's no intensity branch anywhere in the scheduling path to keep in sync. `MusicSys.setIntensity(f)` (real as of this phase; was a no-op stub) ramps each tier-2/3/4 gate toward 0/1 over `MUSIC_LAYER_CROSSFADE` (1.5 s) via `linearRampToValueAtTime` — a ramp, never a jump — **only when its target actually flips** (the `setDuck` idempotency idiom, reused). Tier 1 gates are skipped entirely (always on, bare-set to 1 once at track construction). **Called ONLY from the real `nextWave()`** (`MusicSys.setIntensity(difficultyFactor(game.wave))`, added right after `game.wave++`) — `nextWave()` also runs once at `startGame()`, so a fresh run is correctly pinned to `difficultyFactor(1) === 0` (foundation only) before any gameplay track has even loaded. The per-frame `updateMusic()` path is untouched — no per-frame intensity recompute. **(3) TRACK SELECTION IS WIRED FOR REAL:** `musicStateFor(s)` now returns `settings.musicTrack` (not a generic `"play"`) when `s === "playing"` — since the selected track name IS a `MUSIC_TRACKS` key, a mid-game switch (Options, pause menu) is just an ordinary `setState()` crossfade the next frame `updateMusic()` runs, no separate track-switch code path needed. **(4) PERF (FLAG-9c, the round's flagged biggest risk):** since every layer is always scheduled, per-step node creation is intensity-**independent** — measured (not estimated) via a counting `ctx.createGain`/`createOscillator`/`createBiquadFilter` wrapper driven across a full loop of each track: worst-case nodes for a single scheduled step = **7 (tense)**, **6 (retro)**, **6 (ambient)** — overall worst case **7**, comfortably inside the "handful" budget the prompt set (each note costs 2 nodes — envelope gain + oscillator — or 3 where a layer uses a filter; no track uses oscillator detune, which would have added a 3rd/4th). No restructuring needed. **Tests — extended `scratchpad/test-v34-p6.js` in place** (sections H-N, **+59 assertions, 81→140**), driving the REAL `MusicSys`/`nextWave`/`musicStateFor`/`updateMusic` — no reimplementation: (H) all three tracks `setState`/stop/crossfade without throwing, each building exactly one `layerGate` per layer; (I) at f = 0/0.25/0.5/0.8, exactly 1/2/3/4 layers read `gain.value > 0`, and every threshold crossing (up **and** back down) moves via `linearRampToValueAtTime`, never a bare jump (tier-1's one-time construction-time bare-set to 1 explicitly excluded from that check — correct, not a bug); (J) a real 120-frame run at a fixed wave calls `setIntensity` **zero** times, while a direct `nextWave()` call bumps it by exactly one; (K) for all three tracks, the exact (`layer.name`+pitch) note sequence over a full loop is **byte-identical** at f=0 vs f=1 — direct proof the scheduler never branches on intensity; (L) `musicStateFor` round-trips `title`/`gameover`/`playing`(→`settings.musicTrack`), and flipping `settings.musicTrack` mid-`"playing"` through `updateMusic()` crossfades to a **new** `trackGain` while the old one fades to ~0 (never a hard cut); (M) a **second, fully fresh** script evaluation against an empty `localStorage` confirms `settings.musicTrack === "retro"` out of the box; (N) the per-step node-creation measurement above, asserted bounded (≤16) per track and reported to console. **Full regression re-run green: all 24 test files, 1444 assertions** (up from 1385 — only `test-v34-p6.js` changed, +59; no other file touched, confirming the additive scope held). `node --check` clean on the extracted script. GDD updated in place: **§2.8** (the three tracks + the layer-gating architecture + the perf numbers), **§2.16** (the Music Track row description — no longer "silent stubs"), the Architecture Map (the **MusicSys** row rewritten for `layerGates`/real `setIntensity`), the top Version line, and this entry. Did NOT push.
- **v3.4 (Phase 6 of N)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.4.md` §9a/§9c/§9d, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.4.md`. **P6: the music-system CORE — lookahead scheduler, menu ducking, title track, Options row.** The three gameplay tracks are P7; this phase is the machinery + the title track only. **(1) `MusicSys`, a new module ALONGSIDE `AudioSys`** (not inside it — `AudioSys` is a flat bag of one-shot voices and must not grow a scheduler). Confirmed by grep that `AudioSys.init()` already builds `this.music` as a GainNode wired to master with nothing on its input (a comment said so) — this phase is that future, so the bus was untouched: all `MusicSys` output routes into `AudioSys.music` and the existing Music Volume slider governs it with zero new plumbing. Signal path **note envelopes → per-state `trackGain` (crossfaded) → `MusicSys.duck` → `AudioSys.music`**. **(2) The scheduler** — a standard Web Audio **lookahead**: `MusicSys.update()`, called once per frame from the main loop's new `updateMusic()`, schedules any note whose start falls within `MUSIC_LOOKAHEAD` (0.2 s) of `ctx.currentTime`, stepping a **generic step-sequencer track table** (`{stepDur, steps, layers:[{type,gain,steps:[cell|null]}]}`) — never `setTimeout`/`setInterval`. `scheduleStep` clamps a note's start to `max(stepTime, currentTime)` so a stalled frame can't schedule into the past. **Tracks are DATA**, so P7 adds three more tables without touching the scheduler. **(3) State + ducking** — `setState("title"|"play"|"off")` crossfades (old `trackGain` ramps to silence, new one ramps in), driven each frame off `game.state` (`playing→"play"`, `title→"title"`, else→silence, with game-over fading over ~1 s `MUSIC_FADE_OUT` — a look-call, since the game-over screen is a quiet beat). `setDuck(menuActive())` ramps `duck` to `MUSIC_DUCK_GAIN` (0.5) over `MUSIC_DUCK_RAMP` (0.15 s, `linearRampToValueAtTime`, not a bare set) while any pause-menu screen is open — `menuActive()` ⇔ `game.paused`, which covers Pause/Options/Difficulty/Controls/Achievements, so one line covers the whole §9 ducking spec; `setDuck` is idempotent (only ramps on a change) since it's called every frame. **First-gesture gating**: every entry point is `if (!AudioSys.ctx) return;`-guarded like every `AudioSys` voice, so nothing starts on page load — the title track begins on the first key/button press (and cleanly whenever the player returns to the title after a game, `ctx` already live); the `duck` node is built lazily by `ensureGraph`. **`setIntensity(f)` is a no-op stub** this phase (P7 gates gameplay layers on it). **(4) The title track** — one long, patient, **epic-adventure** synthesized loop (48 s = 96 steps × 0.5 s) via `buildTitleTrack()`: slow build, wide intervals, no percussion pulse, no urgency, deliberately unrelated to the gameplay mood set and **not** layered by difficulty. Five WebAudio layers (low sine bass drone, two detuned triangle pads at root + open fifth, an octave shimmer, a sparse high lead entering in the back half) — no audio files (house standard). **(5) Options menu — a REQUIRED refactor first.** `menuOptions()`/`drawOptionsMenu()` dispatched on **hardcoded row indices** (`m.index <= 2` sliders, `=== 3/4/5/6` for Controls/Achievements/Difficulty/Back), which any inserted row would silently shift. Both were refactored to **dispatch by label** (the `menuRoot()` precedent) as a distinct verified step, then the **Music Track** row was added purely additively — placed after "Master Volume", a left/right cycle over `["Tense","Retro","Ambient"]` (the Difficulty-toggle idiom), rendered with a value column mirroring `drawDifficulty`. **Persistence**: a new additive `settings.musicTrack` field (default `"retro"`, FORK-9) into the **frozen** `afd_settings_v1` key — same additive, no-schema-bump pattern as v3.0 P5's `shotPowerupMode`/`magnetMode`, with a corrupt/unknown value falling back to the default on load. All three gameplay track names are selectable but silent behind them (P7 fills them). **Tests** — new file `scratchpad/test-v34-p6.js` (**81 assertions**), a concrete recording Web Audio stub (mutable `currentTime`, gain-param call recording) driving the REAL `MusicSys`/menu/settings code — no reimplementation: every entry point safe with `AudioSys.ctx === null`; `setDuck` moves the duck gain toward 0.5/1.0 via `linearRampToValueAtTime` (asserted the ramp, not a bare `.value =`) and is idempotent; `menuActive()` ducks on **each** of Pause/Options/Difficulty/Controls/Achievements; `setState` transitions without throwing and stops (fades) the previous track, `"play"`/`"off"` leave a null track (silent stub), same-state is a no-op, and the title track restarts cleanly with `ctx` live; the scheduler driven ~55 s of frames against a controlled `currentTime` schedules **each step exactly once, contiguously (no gaps/dupes), monotonically, never into the past**, covering the full 48 s loop and starting real oscillators; the label-dispatch refactor reaches every existing screen and nudges all three sliders; the Music Track row cycles all three values both directions and only ever lands on known values; and `afd_settings_v1` round-trips every pre-existing field (`vol`, bindings, `shotPowerupMode`, `magnetMode`) **+** `musicTrack`, with the key name asserted and corrupt/missing `musicTrack` tolerated. **Two pre-existing files needed fixture updates** (not regressions) because the additive Options row shifted the indices they hardcoded: `test-f8.js` (Controls now via `MENU_OPTIONS.indexOf("Controls")`) and `test-p4.js` (Achievements likewise; `MENU_OPTIONS` added to its harness return-list). A standalone render smoke confirmed the title-screen draw, the Options menu with the Music Track row across all three values, and 200 play+scheduler+draw frames are crash-free. **Full regression re-run green: all 24 test files, 1385 assertions** (up from 1304 — the new file adds 81; the two fixture fixes are net-neutral). `node --check` clean on the extracted script. GDD updated in place: **§2.8** (the music system, the bus, the scheduler, the ducking rule, the title track), **§2.16** (the Music Track row + the label-dispatch refactor + persistence), the Architecture Map (a new **MusicSys** row + the AudioSys / Menu / Constants / Main-loop rows), the top Version line, and this entry. - **v3.4 (Phase 5 of N)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.4.md` §8, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.4.md`. **P5: the low-health warning — a looping siren + a red directional pointer.** With no hit counter and variable damage, "running low" needed an explicit HP line: a new `LOW_HP_THRESHOLD = 100` (40% of `SHIP_MAX_HP`, "five bad seconds from dead" — FORK-8, confirmed, a playtest knob). The **state** is a pure per-frame read (`game.state === "playing" && !game.ship.dead && game.ship.hp <= LOW_HP_THRESHOLD`) — no stored flag — so it engages/disengages freely and a single Health pickup can clear it. **(1) Audio.** A new `AudioSys.lowhp(on)` follows the exact persistent-voice shape `thrust(on)`/`saucer(on)` already use (stored oscillator + gain, created on `true`, torn down on `false`) — a **gentle** 220 Hz sine, LFO-swept ±18 Hz at a slow 0.6 Hz, low gain (0.05): a warble, not a klaxon, so it reads as "you need health" rather than an alarm to mute. **Teardown was the actual risk** (flagged in the phase prompt as the one trap): the siren is driven from a **single edge-detected site** in `update()` — right after the camera-follow, before any other system runs — comparing the current low-HP state against a new latch `game.lowHpSiren` and calling `AudioSys.lowhp(true/false)` exactly once per transition, never every frame. It's torn down (with the latch cleared) at every site `thrust(false)`/`saucer(false)` already are, grepped and matched one-for-one: `killShip()`, `quitToTitle()`, and `openPause()` — plus reset in `startGame()` so a fresh run never inherits a droning siren. **(2) Visual.** A second red directional chevron, the exact `drawPoly([[7,0],[-4,-4],[-4,4]], …)` shape the dock chevron (§2.10) already uses, orbiting screen-center at radius **58** (the dock's is 42, so both can show without overlapping) in a new `COLOR.lowhp` (`#ff4040` — checked distinct from `COLOR.hp`, `COLOR.clumpHot` #ff5a2a, and the low-HP bar fill #ff7060). It targets the **nearest** live `type === "health"` powerup via a real wrap-aware nearest-scan over `game.powerups` (`dist2`, not find-first — correct if a second Health powerup ever coexists) and points using `angleTo` (wrap-aware, so it's correct across a world-wrap seam where a naive angle would be ~180° wrong). Drawn only while the state is engaged **and** a health powerup exists on the field; hidden otherwise, with nothing to track when it isn't. **FLAG-8a, deliberately left open:** `POWERUP_HEALTH_GAP` (18–26 s ambient spawn cadence) was **not** shortened and no force-spawn was added — a player can be at 40% HP with the siren running and nothing to point at for up to 26 s. Logged for a decision after playtest, not fixed pre-emptively. **Tests** — new file `scratchpad/test-v34-p5.js` (**33 assertions**), driving the REAL `update()`/`damageShip()`/`killShip()`/`quitToTitle()`/`openPause()`/`applyPowerup()`/`draw()` — no reimplementation: constants (`LOW_HP_THRESHOLD === 100`, `COLOR.lowhp` a hex distinct from the three collision colors); the state engages at exactly the threshold and not at threshold+1; a spy on `AudioSys.lowhp` (forwarding to the real implementation so the persistent-voice bookkeeping still runs) proves the siren fires `true` exactly once on the rising edge — not every frame across ten subsequent frames — and `false` exactly once on the falling edge driven by a **real** `applyPowerup("health")` pickup; the teardown assertions (the point of the file): `killShip()`, `quitToTitle()`, and `openPause()` each call `AudioSys.lowhp(false)` exactly once and clear `game.lowHpSiren` when the siren is live going in; the pointer's angle is recovered from a real `draw()` call by recording `ctx.translate`/`ctx.rotate`/`strokeStyle` and matching the segment stroked in `COLOR.lowhp`, confirming it equals `angleTo(ship, powerup)` both in the open field and **across a world-wrap seam** (where the naive `atan2` delta differs by more than 90° from the wrap-aware one — asserted as a sanity check); nearest-selection with two Health powerups on the field targets the nearer by wrap-aware `dist2`; and `draw()` is crash-free with zero/one Health powerup on the field and with the dock chevron also showing. Full regression re-run green: **all 23 test files, 1304 assertions** (up from 1271 — the new file adds 33; no existing file needed a change). Re-ran the pre-existing, documented `test-p5.js` §G flake 20× in isolation post-change (1/20 failed) to confirm it's still the same ~5% RNG-timing flake from prior sessions, not a regression — this phase adds no `rand()` calls to any code path that test exercises. `node --check` clean on the extracted script. - **v3.4 (Phase 4 of N)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.4.md`, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.4.md`. **P4: the Magnet buff — screen-wide range with falloff, 2× duration, pulls clumps.** Five changes, all confirmed against the live build by grep first. **(1) Duration doubled, both expiry modes.** A new `MAGNET_DURATION = POWERUP_DURATION * 2` (**30 s**) — the shared `POWERUP_DURATION` (15) is deliberately left alone so rapid/triple/engine don't double with it. A new `powerDuration(type)` helper mirrors `powerMode(type)`: 30 for magnet, 15 otherwise. **Three call sites**, and the third is the one most easily missed: (a) `applyPowerup` sets `game.powerFx[type] = powerDuration(type)`; (b) the HUD active-effect bar's **denominator** became `game.powerFx[t] / powerDuration(t)` (miss this and the magnet bar renders permanently over-full); (c) `POWERUP_BUDGET` already reads `MAGNET_PIECES`, so pieces-mode doubled for free once `MAGNET_PIECES` went **20→40** (grep-confirmed, not assumed). **(2) Range reaches the top of the screen.** `MAGNET_RANGE_MULT` (the ≈54 px `3 × GARBAGE_PICKUP` reach) is **deleted**; a new flat `MAGNET_RANGE = 380` (px from ship center, deliberately > `VIEW_H/2` = 360 so a piece at the very top of the viewport still feels a pull) — a ~7× buff. `MAGNET_PICKUP_MULT` (the pickup-circle widener, 1.6) is untouched, a different thing. **(3) Strength + quadratic falloff.** `MAGNET_PULL` retuned 360→**520** (px/s² at zero distance) and a new `MAGNET_PULL_MIN = 60` (px/s² floor at max range); in the pull block `t = 1 − d/MAGNET_RANGE` and `accel = MAGNET_PULL_MIN + (MAGNET_PULL − MAGNET_PULL_MIN)·t²` — quadratic, so the near-field yank is dramatic and the far field a nudge; `MAGNET_DAMP` (0.06) unchanged. **(4) All garbage, not just singles.** The `pieces === 1` gate on the pull is removed (v3.3's 9c made clumps directly scoopable, so the v3.2 P1 "you can't hook a clump" justification is dead — the GDD reasoning was rewritten, not left standing). A clump is heavy (`Garbage.mass` sums on merge), so `accel /= Math.sqrt(g.mass)` — **sqrt, not linear** (FORK-6, the 0.5 exponent commented as a playtest knob): a mass-1 single is bit-identically unaffected (√1 = 1), a mass-11 clump pulls at ~30% (drifts toward you but slow enough to outrun/line up — preserves the "heavy clumps are slow anchors" identity). **(5) Magnet budget on a clump scoop (FLAG-7b).** The pieces-mode budget decrement previously lived only in the `pieces === 1` hook branch, so scooping a clump under an active Magnet spent zero budget — a loophole now that clumps are pulled. The clump branch decrements `game.powerBudget.magnet` by `take` (clamped at 0) when the magnet is active and `magnetMode` is `"pieces"`, so a 6-piece clump costs 6 just like 6 singles. **Tests** — extended the files that own the magnet fixtures, all driving the REAL `update()`/`applyPowerup`/pickup loop (no reimplementation): `scratchpad/test-v31-coalesce.js` (the pull physics — 108→124 assertions): a single at 350 px IS pulled and one at 400 px is NOT; the same across a world-wrap seam (naive 2210 px would be out of range — proves `shortDelta`/`dist2`); falloff ≈`MAGNET_PULL` near, ≈`MAGNET_PULL_MIN` (strictly > 0) at max range, monotonic decreasing; a mass-1 single's per-frame Δv is **bit-identical** to the unscaled formula (the √1 = 1 regression guard) and a mass-9 clump's is exactly 1/3; §11's old "a clump feels NO pull" assertion **reversed in place** (with a comment saying it was reversed in v3.4 P4 and why); scooping a 6-clump under a pieces-mode Magnet spends exactly 6 budget; and coalescence (12-piece → Hunter) still fires with the Magnet OFF. `scratchpad/test-p5.js` (the powerup-machinery fixtures — +15): `powerDuration` returns 30/15 by type, `applyPowerup("magnet")` arms 30 in time mode / 40 in pieces mode while the other three stay 15, and the **HUD bar denominator** is verified by driving the REAL `draw()` through a recording canvas and reading the magnet bar's fill width at `powerFx.magnet = 15` (half of 30 → 47 px, not the over-full 94 the old `POWERUP_DURATION` denominator would give). `scratchpad/test-f6.js` swapped its deleted-constant reference and its magnet arm-duration assertion to 30. Full regression re-run green: **all 22 test files, 1271 assertions** (up from 1241). `node --check` clean on the extracted script. GDD updated in place: **§2.14** (range/strength/falloff, the 30 s duration in both modes, the constants callout), **§2.5.1** (the "Magnet ignores clumps" bullet rewritten — it pulls clumps now; the "natural anti-coalescence tool" bullet rewritten — at 380 px it out-ranges the 180 px coalescence pull and dominates the entire visible field for 30 s, flagged as this round's **headline playtest ask**), **§2.10** (the stale "still ignores clumps" line), the Architecture Map (Constants + Flow-functions rows), the top Version line, and this entry. **Playtest ask:** whether a screen-wide, 30-second coalescence lockout makes the Magnet feel powerful or simply erases the salvage-management layer whenever it drops. - **v3.4 (Phase 3 of N)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.4.md`, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.4.md`. **P3: scoop durability + a generated size config + `tools/scoop-lab.html`.** **(1) Durability:** `SCOOP_HITS_PER_LEVEL` **2→5** (a playtest knob, commented in place) — the decay site in `damageShip()` already read the constant, so this is a one-line change; shielded/hit-stun hits still early-return before the decay block, so they still don't count. At 5 hits/level a level-5 scoop survives 25 non-lethal hits; with `SHIP_MAX_HP` 250 and `DMG_MEDIUM` 35 a full-health run only takes ~7 hits before death, so the scoop is now effectively **sticky** once earned — intentional, commented in code so a future session doesn't "fix" it. **(2) The size arrays are now GENERATED, not hand-picked.** New `SHIP_DRAW_W` (18 — the drawn hull's width, confirmed by grep against `Ship.draw()`'s poly) and a new `SCOOP_CONFIG` object (`maxWidthMult: 3.0`, `minWidthMult: 1.2`, `curve: 1.0`, `minDepth: 20`, `maxDepth: 36`) feed a new helper `buildScoopSteps(min, max, curve)`: index 0 is always 0, indices 1..`SCOOP_MAX_LEVEL` interpolate `min` to `max` via `((k-1)/(N-1))**curve` (1.0 = linear, >1 weights growth toward L5). `SCOOP_WIDTH`/`SCOOP_DEPTH` are now `buildScoopSteps(...)` calls instead of literal arrays, but keep the **exact same shape** (6-entry, index = level) — grep-confirmed `inScoopBox()`, `Ship.draw()`'s prong V, and the HUD pip row all index them unchanged, so no downstream reader needed a change. **The load-bearing invariant `SCOOP_WIDTH[0] === 0 && SCOOP_DEPTH[0] === 0`** (so `inScoopBox` returns false at `scoopLevel` 0 and pickup stays byte-identical to the pre-scoop build) is asserted with a `throw` right after the arrays are built, not just left to tests. The generated values (≈21.6/29.7/37.8/45.9/54 width, 20/24/28/32/36 depth) closely resemble but don't exactly reproduce the old hand-picked arrays — expected, no attempt made to force a match. **(3) New file `tools/scoop-lab.html`** — a standalone, self-contained interactive design harness, **not** part of the game build (no imports, no build step; it carries its own duplicate copies of `buildScoopSteps`/`inScoopBox`/`drawPoly`/`glowStroke`/the ship hull poly/the canister draw — accepted duplication, since drift here can only ever produce a bad *preview*, never a bad *build*). Renders the ship (same vector-glow look, scoop prongs in `COLOR.dock` green) with live sliders for all five `SCOOP_CONFIG` fields, a level 0–5 stepper plus a "show all 6 levels" ghost overlay (nested mouths, so the scaling *between* steps is visible at a glance), a draggable scatter of real-size (radius-7) garbage canisters highlighted via the real `inScoopBox` math when inside the mouth (or the base pickup circle), a live readout of the generated arrays, and a "copy config" button that prints the exact `SCOOP_CONFIG` object literal to paste into the game. Deliberately minimal — no thrust, chain, wrap, or clumps; it answers "how big does this look," not "how does this play." **Tests** — extended `scratchpad/test-v33-p3.js` (driving the REAL `inScoopBox`/`damageShip`/`buildScoopSteps` — no reimplementation): `SCOOP_HITS_PER_LEVEL === 5`; `buildScoopSteps` index 0 is 0, index 5 equals max, monotonically increasing, curve 1.0 is exactly linear at the midpoint, curve 2.0 clusters early levels low and makes the last step the biggest; `SCOOP_WIDTH[5] === SCOOP_CONFIG.maxWidthMult * SHIP_DRAW_W` exactly; the level-0-is-byte-identical assertion re-verified against the generated arrays; the 2-hit decay assertions rewritten to 5 (four hits → no drop, five → exactly one level, ten → two levels), shielded/i-frame hits still don't count. Full regression re-run green: **all 22 test files, 1241 assertions** (up from 1222 — `test-v33-p3.js` grew 46→65; no other file needed a change). `node --check` clean on the extracted script. GDD updated in place: **§2.14.1** (the generated-config rewrite, the durability retune + its rationale, the `tools/scoop-lab.html` description), **§2.14**'s constants callout, the Architecture Map Constants row, the top Version line, and this entry. Did NOT push.
- **v3.4 (Phase 2 of N)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.4.md`, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.4.md`. **P2: the difficulty-lever mechanism + the first two levers (powerup size, dock size).** A **difficulty lever** is a small, named, catalogued knob — `{enabled, start, floor}` — that scales one quantity from an easy wave-1 `start` down toward its shipped `floor` along the **existing, shipped** `difficultyFactor`/`ramp` curve; levers deliberately do **not** get their own curve, since `RAMP_WAVES` already governs the whole game's pacing (§2.13). New helper `leverScale(lever, wave)` (next to `ramp` in the Helpers block): `enabled ? Math.max(floor, ramp(start, floor, wave)) : start`. When `enabled` is `false` the lever is **inert** — the quantity is pinned at `start` regardless of wave — so a lever ships fully built, wired into real entity construction, and test-proven to ramp correctly, without changing observed gameplay. `floor` is a **hard clamp**: a lever can only ever bring a quantity back down to today's shipped baseline, never past it — making the game harder than today requires a baseline change, not a lever flip. **Two levers seeded this phase, both `{enabled:false, start:2.0, floor:1.0}`:** `LEVER_POWERUP_SIZE` (scales `Powerup.radius`, next to `POWERUP_RADIUS`) and `LEVER_DOCK_SIZE` (scales `Dock.radius`, next to `DOCK_RADIUS`) — both evaluated **at construction**, not per frame, so ramping only affects newly-spawned powerups / the next wave's dock. **Critical bug caught and fixed as part of this wiring:** the powerup pickup gate in `update()` read the raw `POWERUP_RADIUS` constant (`const r = POWERUP_RADIUS + SHIP_RADIUS`), which would have silently disagreed with the rendered (lever-scaled) hex housing — fixed to `p.radius + SHIP_RADIUS`, confirming render and collision radii are the same number. For the dock, every other read of `DOCK_RADIUS` was grepped and routed through `dock.radius`/`game.dock.radius`: the intake-vane geometry (the `-10` inner ring and the hardcoded `14` inner radius, the latter now scaled proportionally) and the "RECYCLE" label offset (`+22`, likewise scaled), plus the offload-proximity gate (`+10`) and the combo-reset distance (`+40`) — the `+10`/`+40` margins were **deliberately left as absolute px** (feel margins, not geometry). Both levers ship **disabled**, so the only observable effect this phase is that powerups and the recycling dock are now permanently 2× their old size (since `start = 2.0` is pinned). New living doc **`DIFFICULTY-LEVERS.md`** at the repo root (never archived) catalogues the mechanism, the enabled/disabled contract, the floor-as-hard-clamp rule, a lever registry (seeded with these two), the assumptions/decisions above, and a candidate-levers backlog (`HUNTER_GARBAGE` counts, `GARBAGE_DECAY`, `POWERUP_DROP_CHANCE`, `CARGO_GROW_PER`) for future rounds. Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-v34-p2.js`, new, **225 assertions**, driving the REAL `leverScale`/`Powerup`/`Dock`/`update()` — no reimplementation): a disabled lever returns `start` at every wave from 1 to 200; an enabled lever returns `start` at wave 1, decreases monotonically toward `floor` as wave climbs, and never drops below `floor` at any wave up to 200; a `Powerup` built at wave 1 (lever disabled) has `radius === POWERUP_RADIUS * 2`, a canister 40 px away **is** collected at that radius via the real `update()` pickup gate (and a control case at the 1× baseline shows it would **not** be collected at 40 px, proving the gate genuinely reads `p.radius`); a `Dock` built at wave 1 has `radius === DOCK_RADIUS * 2`, its baked octagon `pts` reach that radius (not the raw constant), the real offload gate fires at the scaled distance, and `draw()` is crash-free; flipping each lever's `enabled` to `true` and comparing wave 1 vs wave 100 proves the ramp genuinely shrinks the quantity toward the floor and clamps there — both levers proven to work while shipping disabled, as required. One pre-existing test file needed a fixture update (not a regression): `scratchpad/test-p6.js`'s four hand-built `game.dock` stub objects lacked a `radius` field, so the new `game.dock.radius` reads in `update()` evaluated to `NaN` and broke its dock-delivery-driven assertions (Section B/F) — fixed by adding `radius: DOCK_RADIUS` to each stub (`DOCK_RADIUS` added to that test's own return-list); no game logic changed, confirmed by the fix being purely additive to the test harness. Full regression re-run green: **all 25 test files, 1222 assertions** (up from 997 — the new file adds 225, `test-p6.js`'s existing assertion count unchanged after the fixture fix). `node --check` clean on the extracted script. GDD updated in place: **§2.13** (a new difficulty-levers subsection introducing `leverScale`, pointing at `DIFFICULTY-LEVERS.md` as the registry), **§2.10** (dock-size lever + the routed reads), **§2.14** (powerup-size lever + the pickup-gate fix), the Architecture Map (Constants / Helpers / Entity-classes rows), the top Version line, and this entry. Did NOT push.
- **v3.4 (Phase 1 of N)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.4.md`, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.4.md`. **P1: economy & dock tuning** — three changes, all in `asteroids-deluxe.html`. **(1) Hunter garbage drops scale by tier:** `HUNTER_GARBAGE` (previously a flat `3`, used for both large and medium) and `HUNTER_SMALL_GARBAGE` (previously `6` at the small tier) are replaced by one per-tier table shaped like `HUNTER_RADII`/`HUNTER_SCORE`/`HUNTER_DAMAGE`: `HUNTER_GARBAGE = {3:3, 2:2, 1:1}` (canisters per kill, by tier). `HUNTER_SMALL_MASS` (0.5) is **kept** — the small tier's single canister is still low-mass scrap with the paler tint. `destroyHunter` reads `HUNTER_GARBAGE[h.size]` in **both** branches (the small-tier branch and the large/medium branch); score, the 3-way split, the small-tier `maybeDropPowerup`, and the fan-out kick ranges are all unchanged. A full 13-member lineage (1 large → 3 medium → 9 small) now emits `3 + 3·2 + 9·1` = **18** canisters (9 normal-mass + 9 low-mass, mass 13.5 total) — down from the flat-rate era's 66/39. **`DEBRIS_GARBAGE` bumped 3→4** in the same commit (a playtest knob, commented as such) to compensate field-side for the Hunter-side cut, so total field supply lands close to the pre-P1 level while Hunter drops still scale by tier. Both `HUNTER_GARBAGE` and `DEBRIS_GARBAGE` are marked playtest knobs in code — field density is the thing most likely to be wrong after this change. **(2) Dock intake rate:** the dock-offload block in `update()` had a bare literal `game.offloadTimer = 0.13;` — hoisted into the constants block as `DOCK_OFFLOAD_INTERVAL = 0.05` (a playtest knob, next to the other `DOCK_*` values) and read at the one assignment site. Nothing else in that block changed — scoring, cargo-cap growth, and every achievement latch stay keyed to the same per-canister events. **(3) Tow capacity 20→24:** `CARGO_CAP_MAX` raised 20→24. `CARGO_THRUST`/`CARGO_MAXSPD`/`CARGO_MASS` were **deliberately not re-solved** — a bigger hold is *supposed* to cost handling (m=24 lands at ~41% thrust / ~58% top speed, vs ~45%/63% at the old m=20 ceiling); the tug's `massFactor = min(1.4, m·0.07)` already saturates at m≈20, so it doesn't get worse at m=24. This one was treated as load-bearing, not just an edit: GDD §3.4's chain-stability envelope (validated at 20 nodes / `CHAIN_ITER` 4) was re-validated at the new 24-node cap via a headless stress driving the **real** `updateChain()` — a 24-node chain, hard thrust-flips across a world wrap, 900 frames — asserting no NaN in any node position, no velocity blowup, and reporting worst-case link stretch on the 20 px `CHAIN_LINK`. Measured: **4.11 px at `CHAIN_ITER` 4** (and 3.67 px at 5, for comparison) — both comfortably under the ~5 px budget, so `CHAIN_ITER` stayed at **4**, no bump needed. Also confirmed by grep (unchanged): Heavy Hauler / Freight Baron / The Long Haul all still latch on the literal `game.deliveryCount === 12`, not on `game.cargoMax` — they stay decoupled from the growing cap. Tests extended in the existing owning files (no new test file), driving the real `destroyHunter`/`update()`/`updateChain` — no reimplementation: `scratchpad/test-v31-coalesce.js` (sections 17–20, rewritten from the old flat-66 totals to the new per-tier `HUNTER_GARBAGE[size]` totals — 109 assertions, all passing) and `scratchpad/test-f5.js` (the Hunter-lineage/garbage-count sections rewritten the same way — 47 assertions). `scratchpad/test-f3.js`'s Debris-lineage total updated to `13 * DEBRIS_GARBAGE` (52, was the hardcoded 39). `scratchpad/test-p6.js` (the owning cargo/dock/chain-stability test) extended: config asserts updated to `CARGO_CAP_MAX === 24`; the cap-growth loop driven out to 400 deliveries (ceiling now reached at 360 delivered, not 240) with `capAt[360] === 24`; a new assertion that a 25th canister is refused at the new cap; the mass-penalty measurements (`D`) recomputed at m=24 (~41%/58%, Engine-at-24 ≡ plain-12); the momentum-tug massFactor confirmed still capped at 1.4 for both m=20 and m=24; the stability stress (`E`) driven at 24 nodes with the ~5 px budget assertion and the measured 4.11 px reported in the console output; and a new section (`F`) driving a full 24-node chain through real dock deliveries at `DOCK_OFFLOAD_INTERVAL` to confirm it fully offloads, one canister per interval tick (43 assertions total, up from the prior file's count). Full regression re-run green: **all 21 test files, 997 assertions** (up from 991). `node --check` clean on the extracted script. GDD updated in place: **§2.5** (the "every tier emits garbage" bullet rewritten for the per-tier table), **§2.5.1** (the "12-in/66-out amplifier" arithmetic corrected to 12-in/18-out, ~1.5× not ~5.5×; the v3.3 P4 9b rationale — decay is the governor, not emission suppression — explicitly preserved as still holding), **§2.4** (`DEBRIS_GARBAGE` 3→4, 52-canister lineage total), **§2.10/§2.10.1/§2.10.2** (the new cap, the `DOCK_OFFLOAD_INTERVAL` constant, the m=24 handling numbers, the re-validated-not-assumed stability framing), **§3.4** (the stability envelope revalidated at 24 nodes, `CHAIN_ITER` confirmed unchanged), **§4 backlog** (logged "rectangular dock capture geometry" as considered-and-declined for this round), the Architecture Map (Constants / Chain physics / Flow-functions rows), the top Version line, and this entry. Did NOT push.
- **v3.3 (Phase 4 of 4 — round complete)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.3.md` §9, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.3.md`. **P4: the pacing pass** (Changeset-4 items 9a, 9b, 9c) — deliberately **reverses three shipped v3.2 rules** (Paul signed off on all three), re-tuning the coalescence economy so the salvage layer stays dense and churny without silting up. **9a — single garbage decays again** (reverses v3.2 P3's "garbage is permanent"): `GARBAGE_DECAY` (≈ **22 s**) is reintroduced on `Garbage`, counted down in `update()` **only while `pieces === 1`** — a **clump never decays** (FORK-4, resolved: no; a clump is a target *and* a scoopable pickup, so aging it out would steal loot + the Hunter-prevention window). At 0 the single dies; `draw()` blinks it out over its last `GARBAGE_FADE` (≈ 2 s). Chain nodes never decay (they're `game.chain`, not `game.garbage`); severed garbage (`Garbage.fromNode`) is a single and inherits the same **one** `GARBAGE_DECAY` (the deleted `GARBAGE_SEVER_DECAY` stays deleted). Re-tuned around the shorter single life: **`GARBAGE_COALESCE_DELAY` 6.0→3.0** (6.0 was tuned *for* permanent garbage; a third of a 22 s life spent inert meant nothing clumped) and **`GARBAGE_MAGNET_RANGE` 260→180** (260 was raised only because garbage was permanent) — all three playtest knobs, commented as such. **9b — every Hunter drops garbage** (reverses v3.2 P3's FORK-B/B1): the `const emitGarbage = !h.bornOfScrap;` gate in `destroyHunter` is deleted, and the **`HunterSatellite.bornOfScrap` field + its split-child propagation are deleted entirely** (FORK-5, resolved: yes — it was read by nothing else; `game.stats.hunterCoalesced` is bumped at the coalescence transform and never read the flag, so **Waste Not is untouched** — verified). Every Hunter of every origin now emits at its tier counts (3 / 3 / 6-at-low-mass), so a coalesced lineage drops the full 66 like a timer-spawned one. This **reopens the 12-in / up-to-66-out amplifier** B1 had closed — intentional: 9a's single-decay is the governor now, a single visible universal lever instead of hidden per-lineage plumbing. **9c — clumps are scoopable** (reverses v3.2 P1's "un-hookable"): in the pickup pass, a `pieces > 1` clump entering the capture region (base `GARBAGE_PICKUP` circle **OR** the P3 scoop box — **unconditional**, no `scoopLevel` gate; FORK-6, resolved: no) with chain room is scooped — `take = min(cargoMax − chain.length, pieces)` nodes are pushed at the clump's per-piece mass; if the whole clump fit it dies (mass conserved onto the chain), else the leftover survives with `pieces`/`mass`/`radius` re-derived, `coalesceDelay` re-armed, cached hull regenerated, and an outward **`SCOOP_SPILL_KICK`** (≈ 85 px/s) kick away from the ship. Scooping is **lossy but instant** (a 3-slot chain scooping a 10-clump banks 3, wastes 7); **shatter (v3.2 P2) survives as the lossless tool** (all pieces become hookable singles). The Magnet still ignores clumps (`pieces === 1` gate); a partial scoop can only happen when the chain fills, so the leftover can't be re-scooped (no cooldown needed). Headless-tested through the REAL `update()`/`coalesceGarbage`/`destroyHunter`/pickup pass — no reimplementation — with `scratchpad/test-v31-coalesce.js` **rewritten**, not extended: its old `bornOfScrap`-emits-ZERO assertions now assert the **inverse** (a scrap-born lineage emits the full 66; `bornOfScrap` is absent from the source at every generation), and new sections cover single-decay-at-`GARBAGE_DECAY` vs clumps-never-decay, chain-nodes-never-decay, `GARBAGE_DECAY > GARBAGE_COALESCE_DELAY` by a wide margin (the relationship, not just the values), scooping a 5-clump with room (5 nodes, mass conserved), a partial scoop of a 10-clump into 3 slots (3 nodes + a live 7-piece leftover with re-derived radius/mass, re-armed delay, outward kick, and no immediate re-scoop), scooping at `scoopLevel 0` via the circle AND through the box, and Waste Not still keying on `hunterCoalesced` — **80 → 109 assertions**. `test-f3.js` fixed in place (severed garbage now inherits `GARBAGE_DECAY` again, not "no decay field"). Full regression re-run green: **all 21 test files, 991 assertions** (up from 962 — coalesce +29; `node --check` clean; the one long-run decay test isolates ambient hazards each frame, as `test-firerate` does, so it can't flake). GDD updated in place: **§2.10.1** (the load-bearing "decay protects readability / density held without decay" bullet **rewritten** — decay is back, with the full history of why the v3.2 removal was superseded so a future session doesn't re-remove it), **§2.5.1** (clumps scoopable, `bornOfScrap` gone, shatter=lossless vs scoop=lossy, the two-tools-one-fulcrum framing, the retuned constants), **§2.10** (single decay + the scoop-clump collection rule), **§2.5** (every Hunter drops garbage), §2.7 wave-count note, the perf/playtest-risk asks, the Architecture Map rows (Constants / Entity classes / game-object / Flow-functions / update(dt)), the top Version line, and this entry. Did NOT push. **v3.3 is complete** — next housekeeping per `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.3.md`: archive both v3.3 planning docs (version-suffixed) and rename the legacy bare `archive/IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES.md` → `-v2.md`; the open `nextWave` count / `SPAWN_MAX_DIST` lull lever remains available if playtest shows the pacing pass didn't fully land it.
- **v3.3 (Phase 3 of 4)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.3.md`, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.3.md`. **P3: the Scoop powerup + the weighted powerup drop economy** (Changeset-4 items 8 and 6). **PART A — drop economy:** `POWERUP_DROP_CHANCE` 0.10→0.16 and `POWERUP_DECAY` 14→26 s (both commented playtest knobs); the flat pick in `maybeDropPowerup` is replaced by a **weighted** roll over a new, **separate** table `POWERUP_DROP_WEIGHTS = {rapid: 3, triple: 3, scoop: 2, magnet: 1, engine: 1}` (favors the shot powerups). Critically, `POWERUP_DROP_TYPES` — which the HUD active-effect row / `powerActive`/`powerMode`/`powerBudget` iterate as the list of *timed* effects — is **left untouched** (Scoop is persistent, not timed, and is NOT added to it; FLAG A-9). **PART B — the Scoop:** the first **persistent, non-timed** ship upgrade here. New state `game.scoopLevel` (0..`SCOOP_MAX_LEVEL` = 5) + `game.scoopHits`, both reset in `startGame()`, **not** in `powerFx`/`powerBudget`. A new droppable `"scoop"` type gets its own `drawPowerupGlyph` funnel/V case and a `POWERUP_COLOR.scoop` violet (no other purple in the palette, so it never reads as a hazard tell); `applyPowerup("scoop")` raises `scoopLevel` by 1 (capped, `"SCOOP +1"` float), or at the cap pays a `SCOOP_MAX_BONUS` (500) score bonus + `"SCOOP MAX"` float (mirrors the full-HP milestone). **Geometry (FORK-2 resolved: an oriented box, not a circle):** `SCOOP_WIDTH = [0,22,30,38,46,54]` and `SCOOP_DEPTH = [0,20,24,28,32,36]` px (index = level; L5 width 54 = 3× the ship's 18 px). The capture lives in the existing pickup pass via `inScoopBox(g)`: rotate the wrap-aware `shortDelta` ship→garbage vector into ship-local space and capture if `|lateral| ≤ SCOOP_WIDTH[lvl]/2` AND `−SHIP_RADIUS ≤ forward ≤ SCOOP_DEPTH[lvl]`. It is **OR'd with the base `GARBAGE_PICKUP` circle** (which always still applies, so `scoopLevel 0` is byte-identical to the pre-scoop build), and `MAGNET_PICKUP_MULT` keeps multiplying the **circle only** (no double-count). **Decay by damage:** in `damageShip()`, on any non-lethal hit (after HP/knockback), `scoopHits++`; at `SCOOP_HITS_PER_LEVEL` (2) it drops one level, resets the tally, floats `"SCOOP −1"`, and plays a new `AudioSys.scooploss()` cue. No time decay; a shielded/i-frame hit early-returns and never counts; the tally doesn't reset on a scoop pickup (FORK-3: no) or accumulate at level 0. **Render:** `Ship.draw()` draws two prongs (an open `drawPoly` V in `COLOR.dock` green) from the nose out to ±width/2 at the mouth depth, before the hull, when `scoopLevel > 0`. **HUD:** a `SCOOP` 5-pip row (violet, under the powerup rows, hidden at level 0), drawn *outside* the timed-effect loop. **Known/accepted:** `applyPowerup` increments `game.stats.powerupsPicked`, so picking a scoop freezes the `maxWaveNoPowerup` "No Powerups Needed" achievement — correct, it IS a powerup (FLAG A-8). Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-v33-p3.js`, new, **46 assertions**, driving the REAL `update()`/`damageShip()`/`applyPowerup`/`maybeDropPowerup` — no reimplementation): constants + the two-table separation (scoop absent from `POWERUP_DROP_TYPES`, present in `POWERUP_DROP_WEIGHTS`); scoop level climbs 0→5, caps, and pays the bonus at max; the box captures a canister outside `GARBAGE_PICKUP` but inside the mouth at six headings AND across both world wrap seams; canisters behind the ship, laterally outside the mouth, or beyond depth are NOT captured; at `scoopLevel 0` the pickup set is identical to the circle-only build; two non-lethal hits drop exactly one level, four drop two, hits at level 0 are harmless; a shielded and an i-frame hit do NOT count toward `scoopHits`; `maybeDropPowerup` only ever yields weighted types (scoop drops, Health never does). Full regression re-run green: **all 21 test files, 962 assertions** (up from 916 — the new file adds 46; no existing test needed a change, confirming the additive scope held). A render smoke (draw()/prongs/pips/glyph/`scooploss` at several levels) is crash-free; `node --check` clean on the extracted script. GDD updated in place: §2.10 (collection mouth), §2.12 (scoop decay on damage), §2.14 + new **§2.14.1** (the persistent-upgrade category), the Architecture Map (Constants / game-object / Flow-functions / AudioSys / draw() rows), the top Version line, and this entry. Did NOT push. - **v3.3 (Phase 2 of 4)** — specs in `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.3.md`, build order in `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.3.md`. **P2: real satellite line art for the Debris Satellites** (Changeset-4 items 2 and 5) — scope was `DebrisSatellite` only; the Hunter's diamond is untouched (it's the threat tell — FORK-1 resolved: no). A new module-level **`SAT_ART`** table holds **six original, wrecked satellite silhouettes** — comms bus + twin solar panels (one panel snapped), dish relay (drooping/cracked dish), boxy Earth-observer with an instrument boom (one panel hanging), a Sputnik-ish sphere with radial whip antennas (one bent), a cylindrical spent booster (dented, flared nozzle), and a truss/array segment (snapped rail) — each an `{ full, small }` pair of polyline arrays in **unit space** (every coord inside the radius-1 circle), each polyline tagged `{ pts, closed }`, drawn through the existing `drawPoly`/`glowStroke` at `this.radius` in `COLOR.debris`. **No fills, no new render primitive, no external assets** — these are authored in code, evoking real archetypes but not traced/imported (FLAG A-7; the file stays a self-contained GPL-3.0 HTML). `DebrisSatellite` now picks one archetype per instance (`this.art = SAT_ART[floor(rand(0, SAT_ART.length))]`; splits re-roll independently) and bakes a per-instance copy **once** in the constructor — scaled to `radius` with a small random per-vertex jitter (~0.045·radius) for the "no two alike / wrecked" look, never re-randomized per frame — replacing the old procedural `hull` + `shards` fields entirely; `draw()` iterates `this.art`, rotated by the **preserved** random `this.angle` + `this.spin` (item 5: nothing anchors art to a fixed "up"). **Small-tier legibility gate:** the small tier (`radius = 13`) draws each archetype's simplified `small` variant (2–4 strokes) instead of `full`, since a 10+ segment design is mush at that size — a look-call, tuned by eye. `this.radius`/`DEBRIS_RADII` and collision are unchanged (art is cosmetic — GDD §3.1); the title screen's decorative `titleDebris` gets the new art for free. Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-v33-p2.js`, new, **28 assertions**, driving the REAL class/table — no reimplementation): `SAT_ART` is 5–6 entries, each `full`+`small` an array of `{ pts:[[x,y]…], closed:bool }` with every unit-space coord inside the radius-1 circle; a fresh `DebrisSatellite` of each size has a non-empty baked `art`, a random `angle` in `[0,TAU)` and `spin` in `[-1.2,1.2]` (a 40-instance spread confirms the rotation is per-instance random, not anchored, and tumbles both ways); `draw()` is crash-free at all three sizes; the small variant is ≤ its `full` in polyline count and per-instance jitter makes instances differ (a baked copy, not the shared `SAT_ART` reference); `hull`/`shards` are gone. **Also hardened `test-firerate.js`** (a pre-existing test-isolation flake, not a code change): section D counts fire-cadence volleys over 1 s of real `update()` but didn't clear ambient hazards, so a wave-1 debris/saucer drifting into the stationary test ship could land a hit whose hit-stun interrupted firing and dropped the count — a rare RNG-timing flake (~0.7% on HEAD) whose rate rides on the shared `Math.random` sequence, so P2's extra per-instance constructor `rand()` calls lifted it to ~4%. The fix clears `game.debris`/`hunters`/`saucers` each frame exactly as it already clears `game.bullets` — the test's own stated intent is to isolate *cooldown-driven* cadence — taking it to 0/250 flakes; no game logic changed. Full regression re-run green: **all 20 test files, 916 assertions** (up from 888 — the new file adds 28). `node --check` clean on the extracted script. GDD updated in place: §2.4 (the Shape bullet — SAT_ART supersedes the procedural silhouette), the Architecture Map (Constants + Entity classes rows), the top Version line, and this entry. - **v3.3 (Phase 1 of 4)** — **P1: the presentation pass** (Changeset-4 items 1, 3, 4, 7) — render/strings only, no sim/collision/constant touched. **(1) Renamed** "Asteroid Field Deluxe" → **"Orbital Overhaul"** throughout: the `<title>` tag, the header banner comment's first line (version-log body kept), the title screen ("ASTEROID FIELD" / "D E L U X E" → "ORBITAL" / "O V E R H A U L", same sizes/colors/positions), and the GDD file itself (`asteroid-field-deluxe-GDD.md` → **`orbital-overhaul-GDD.md`**, H1 + this Version line updated, plus `CLAUDE.md`'s doc-layer pointer and `STATUS.md`'s H1 + design-authority reference). The two `localStorage` keys (`afd_settings_v1`, `afd_achievements_v2`) are **deliberately NOT renamed** — the `afd_` prefix is frozen (an in-code comment now sits at each declaration) because renaming either would silently wipe every player's saved settings/bindings/lifetime achievement tiers on their next load. **(2) Dialogs are now opaque** — `menuPanel()` previously only `strokeRect`'d its panel, so the world showed through and text was hard to read; it now fills first (`rgba(2,6,14,0.95)`), then strokes as before. All five menu screens (root/options/difficulty/controls/achievements) route through `menuPanel`, so one edit fixed all five. `drawMenu()`'s full-screen backdrop dim was also raised `rgba(4,10,20,0.74)` → `~0.88` (the achievements screen's own redundant backdrop fill, drawn on top, matched to the same value). Both alphas are commented as look-call playtest knobs. **(3) Clump silhouette** — `Garbage.draw()` at `pieces > 1` now takes a completely different branch from `pieces === 1` (which stays byte-identical): ONE closed hull polygon (7–9 vertices, jittered around the derived `radius = 7·√pieces`) replaces the old mini-canister cluster (v3.2 P1), because playtest read the cluster as "a pile of pickups" rather than "a target." The hull is generated **once** by a new `makeClumpHull(radius)` helper and **cached** on `this.hull` — set in the constructor, regenerated only at merge time inside `coalesceGarbage` (never per frame) — and rotated live by `this.spin` so it still tumbles. A new `lerpColor()` helper tints the hull from `COLOR.garbage` toward a new **`COLOR.clumpHot`** (`#ff5a2a`, chosen clear of every other hazard hue — FLAG A-7b) as `pieces / HUNTER_COALESCE_COUNT → 1`, so the clump visibly reddens as it nears the Hunter transform — a free threat meter. The radioactive alpha flicker and `glowStroke` are kept; `shatterClump`/`coalesceGarbage`'s merge math are untouched. **(4) LEVEL in the HUD** — the existing `WAVE n` top-right readout (22px, `COLOR.dim` — technically present but too dim/small/cornered to read) is gone, replaced by **`LEVEL n`** at 22px `COLOR.text` in the left column directly under the HULL bar (CARGO/TARGETS/the powerup row's `prow` start all shifted down ~22px to make room). Display label only — `game.wave`, `nextWave()`, `difficultyFactor(wave)`, `ramp(...)`, and every achievement reading `game.wave` are all unchanged; "level" is the player-facing word, "wave" stays the code term (both documented in §2.7 so the vocabularies don't drift). Headless-tested (`scratchpad/test-v33-p1.js`, new, **16 assertions**): `menuPanel` calls `fillRect` before `strokeRect` (an instrumented recording canvas ctx asserts call order) and still returns `{x,y}`; `Garbage.draw()` is crash-free at `pieces` 1, 2, and 11; the cached hull is stable (same array reference and point values) across five repeated `draw()` calls and regenerates (new reference, re-derived radius) after a real merge driven through `coalesceGarbage`; the `pieces===1` branch stays crash-free and untouched; `COLOR.clumpHot` exists as a hex color distinct from `COLOR.garbage`. Full regression (all 19 test files, **888 assertions**) re-run green — no other test file needed adjustment. GDD updated in place: §2.5.1 (clump render — marked superseded, new description), §2.7 (LEVEL/wave vocabulary split), §2.16 (dialog opacity), the Architecture Map (Constants/Entity classes/`draw()` rows), the top Version line, and this entry. Next up per `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.3.md`: **P2 — real satellite line art for `DebrisSatellite`** (independent of P1; blocked on FORK-1 sign-off, recommendation: no Hunter art change).
